{"code":1,"isDone":false,"toInsertArticleList":[{"createdTime":"2020-08-25 08:46:09","updatedTime":"2020-08-25 08:46:09","title":"A new wave of AR Realism with the ARCore Depth API","link":"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/GDBcode/~3/qc14lD9v2Ts/a-new-wave-of-ar-realism-with-arcore-depth-api.html","description":"<meta name=\"twitter:image\" content=\"\"><img style=\"display:none\" src=\"\"> <p><em>Posted by Rajat Paharia, Product Lead, AR Platform</em></p> <p>Since the launch of ARCore, our developer platform for building augmented reality (AR) experiences, we've been focused on providing APIs that help developers seamlessly blend the digital and physical worlds. </p><p>At the end of last year, we announced a preview of the <a href=\"https://developers.googleblog.com/2019/12/blending-realities-with-arcore-depth-api.html\">ARCore Depth API</a>, which uses our depth-from-motion algorithms to generate a depth map with a single RGB camera. Since then, we’ve been working with select collaborators to explore how depth can be used across a range of use cases to enhance AR realism. </p><p>Today, we're taking a major step forward and announcing the Depth API is available in ARCore 1.18 for Android and Unity, including AR Foundation, across hundreds of millions of compatible Android devices. </p><div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\"><a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-bhpSif30EY0/XvOSjkrC7lI/AAAAAAAAI_4/YfBjSqZWzu0SpbyGt6Pzpfs0mhDmq4f7QCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/E714_DepthLab_DepthMap_v01.gif\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"653\" data-original-width=\"300\" height=\"320\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-bhpSif30EY0/XvOSjkrC7lI/AAAAAAAAI_4/YfBjSqZWzu0SpbyGt6Pzpfs0mhDmq4f7QCLcBGAsYHQ/s320/E714_DepthLab_DepthMap_v01.gif\" style=\"width:200px\" /></a><a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-g5DoeNzZh-Y/XvOSrPtYyCI/AAAAAAAAI_8/Of_8YwymbVs7srF6uKfkOoMhrcLiN4_DwCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/depth2.gif\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"512\" data-original-width=\"235\" height=\"320\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-g5DoeNzZh-Y/XvOSrPtYyCI/AAAAAAAAI_8/Of_8YwymbVs7srF6uKfkOoMhrcLiN4_DwCLcBGAsYHQ/s320/depth2.gif\" style=\"width:200px\"/></a></div><p id=\"imgCaption\">Generate a depth map without specialized hardware to unlock capabilities like occlusion</p> <p>As we highlighted last year, a key capability of the Depth API is occlusion: <i>the ability for digital objects to accurately appear behind real world objects</i>. This makes objects feel as if they’re actually in your space, creating a more realistic AR experience. </p> <p>Illumix, the game studio behind <i>Five Nights at Freddy’s AR: Special Delivery</i>, uses occlusion to deepen the realism of the experience by allowing certain characters to hide behind objects for more startling jump scares. </p> <center><a href=\"https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-yJWG16owct8/XvOdT--HdEI/AAAAAAAAJBE/7uCA2AceI_gW71JpGz7SitICaii39Wz9QCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/E714_FNAF_v01.gif\" imageanchor=\"1\" ><img border=\"0\" style=\"width:200px\" src=\"https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-yJWG16owct8/XvOdT--HdEI/AAAAAAAAJBE/7uCA2AceI_gW71JpGz7SitICaii39Wz9QCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/E714_FNAF_v01.gif\" data-original-width=\"300\" data-original-height=\"653\" /></a></center><p id=\"imgCaption\"><a href=\"https://play.google.com/store/apps/details?id=com.illumix.fnafar&hl=en_US\">Play Five Nights at Freddy’s AR: Special Delivery</a></p> <p>While occlusion is an important capability, the ARCore Depth API unlocks more ways to increase realism and enables new interaction types. The <i>ARCore Depth Lab</i> spurred more ideas on how depth can be used, including realistics physics, surface interactions, environmental traversal, and more. Developers can now build on these ideas through the open sourced <a href=\"https://github.com/googlesamples/arcore-depth-lab/\">GitHub project</a>. </p><center><a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-ODisk6SAibc/XvOd-BvL9oI/AAAAAAAAJBM/zVH-1RTIeO0paJPTOc6sqMRNiCWQrRrFgCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/E714_DepthLab_v01.gif\" imageanchor=\"1\" ><img style=\"width:200px\" border=\"0\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-ODisk6SAibc/XvOd-BvL9oI/AAAAAAAAJBM/zVH-1RTIeO0paJPTOc6sqMRNiCWQrRrFgCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/E714_DepthLab_v01.gif\" data-original-width=\"300\" data-original-height=\"653\" /></a></center><p id=\"imgCaption\"><a href=\"https://play.google.com/store/apps/details?id=com.google.ar.unity.arcore_depth_lab\">Experiment with ARCore Depth Lab on the Google Play Store</a></p><p>The designers and engineers at Snap Inc. integrated several of these ideas into a set of <i>Snapchat</i> Lenses including the <i>Dancing Hotdog</i> and a new Android exclusive <i>Undersea World</i> Lens.</p><div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\"><a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-G-C6BbEIeCE/XvOaGb7TU0I/AAAAAAAAJAg/Tr9Jl53P_EsTpwlzOMwVqV76IbtX6xlnQCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/E714_Snapchat_Hotdog_v02.gif\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"653\" data-original-width=\"300\" height=\"320\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-G-C6BbEIeCE/XvOaGb7TU0I/AAAAAAAAJAg/Tr9Jl53P_EsTpwlzOMwVqV76IbtX6xlnQCLcBGAsYHQ/s320/E714_Snapchat_Hotdog_v02.gif\" width=\"147\" style=\"width:200px\"/></a><a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-NHDalcdo4S8/XvOaMuu6JZI/AAAAAAAAJAk/gFnmi44e1PYdHW0vgsxYeLwu4BzdPEEqACLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/E714_Snapchat_Underwater_v02.gif\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"653\" data-original-width=\"300\" height=\"320\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-NHDalcdo4S8/XvOaMuu6JZI/AAAAAAAAJAk/gFnmi44e1PYdHW0vgsxYeLwu4BzdPEEqACLcBGAsYHQ/s320/E714_Snapchat_Underwater_v02.gif\" width=\"147\" style=\"width:200px\"/></a></div><p id=\"imgCaption\"><a href=\"https://play.google.com/store/apps/details?id=com.snapchat.android&hl=en_US\">See how depth can add a layer of realism to your Snapchat experience</a></p><p>Snapchat Lens Creators can now download an ARCore Depth API <a href=\"https://lensstudio.snapchat.com/templates/world/depth-enabled-templates/\">template</a> to create depth-based experiences for compatible Android devices. Sam Hare, Research Engineering Manager at Snap Inc, expressed his excitement, “We’re beginning to understand what kinds of depth capabilities are exciting for developers to build with. This single integration point streamlines and simplifies the development process and enables Lens Studio developers to easily take advantage of advanced depth capabilities.” </p><p>Another app that combines occlusion with other depth capabilities is <i><a href=\"https://experiments.withgoogle.com/linesofplay\">Lines of Play</a></i>, an Android experiment from the Google Creative Lab. Lines of Play lets users create domino art in AR, and uses depth information to showcase both occlusion and collisions. Design elaborate domino creations, topple them over and watch them collide with the furniture and walls in your room. </p><center><a href=\"https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-6kqGGJGrloo/XvOehk_gxxI/AAAAAAAAJBU/xWbMM1vgMo4KmdUUETxZ7HnB9Vm4npaVQCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/unnamed.gif\" imageanchor=\"1\" ><img style=\"width:200px\" border=\"0\" src=\"https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-6kqGGJGrloo/XvOehk_gxxI/AAAAAAAAJBU/xWbMM1vgMo4KmdUUETxZ7HnB9Vm4npaVQCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/unnamed.gif\" data-original-width=\"235\" data-original-height=\"512\" /></a></center> <p id=\"imgCaption\"><a href=\"https://play.google.com/store/apps/details?id=com.arexperiments.dominoes\">Watch as domino pieces topple into each other and onto your walls with Lines of Play</a></p> <p>In addition to gaming and self-expression, depth can also be used to unlock new utility use cases. For example, the <i>TeamViewer Pilot</i> app, a remote assistance solution that enables AR annotations on video calls, uses depth to better understand the environment so experts around the world can more precisely apply real time 3D AR annotations for remote support and maintenance. </p><center><a href=\"https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-G60-ucEZpZM/XvOexUJHNcI/AAAAAAAAJBY/FGHISPdamEQplkAh3BietMRuI-f55zMjQCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/E714_TeamViewer_PilotAlt_v01.gif\" imageanchor=\"1\" ><img style=\"width:200px\" border=\"0\" src=\"https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-G60-ucEZpZM/XvOexUJHNcI/AAAAAAAAJBY/FGHISPdamEQplkAh3BietMRuI-f55zMjQCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/E714_TeamViewer_PilotAlt_v01.gif\" data-original-width=\"300\" data-original-height=\"653\" /></a></center><p id=\"imgCaption\"><a href=\"https://play.google.com/store/apps/details?id=com.teamviewer.pilot&hl=en_US\">3D annotations help experts accurately highlight details in the TeamViewer Pilot app</a></p> <p>Later this year, you will be able to try more depth-enabled AR experiences such as <i>SKATRIX</i> by Reality Crisis and <i>SPLASHAAR</i> by ForwARdgames, that use surface interactions and environmental traversal as they make rich use of the environment around you.</p> <div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\"><a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-25aUjDU487I/XvObrZBoFgI/AAAAAAAAJAw/hPjH7wq4EgIv-vGrneBsBqRPeSZod8Z5gCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/E714_Skatrix_Clip1_v02.gif\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"653\" data-original-width=\"300\" height=\"320\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-25aUjDU487I/XvObrZBoFgI/AAAAAAAAJAw/hPjH7wq4EgIv-vGrneBsBqRPeSZod8Z5gCLcBGAsYHQ/s320/E714_Skatrix_Clip1_v02.gif\" width=\"147\" style=\"width:200px\" /></a><a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-EHoh_ll2Lnw/XvOcYb76r-I/AAAAAAAAJA4/IhRO9qriKE4wGzOySJ49ssglRGy6ePkMgCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/E714_ForwARd_Splash_v01.gif\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"675\" data-original-width=\"310\" height=\"320\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-EHoh_ll2Lnw/XvOcYb76r-I/AAAAAAAAJA4/IhRO9qriKE4wGzOySJ49ssglRGy6ePkMgCLcBGAsYHQ/s320/E714_ForwARd_Splash_v01.gif\" width=\"146\" style=\"width:200px\" /></a></div><p id=\"imgCaption\">Check out surface interactions and environmental traversal  in <a href=\"https://realitycrisis.io/\">SKATRIX</a>, and <a href=\"https://www.forwardgamear.com/\">SPLASHAAR</a></p><p>While depth sensors, such as time-of-flight (ToF) sensors, are not required for the Depth API to work, having them will further improve the quality of experiences. Dr. Soo Wan Kim, Camera Technical Product Manager at Samsung commented on the future that the Depth API and ToF unlocks saying, “Depth will enrich user's AR experience in many perspectives. It will reduce scanning time, and can detect planes fast, even low textured planes. These will bring seamless experiences to users who will be able to use AR apps more easily and frequently.” In the coming months, Samsung will update their <i>Quick Measure</i> app to use the ARCore Depth API on the Galaxy Note10+ and Galaxy S20 Ultra. </p><center><a href=\"https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-cAhz058s0KQ/XvOlO3yw8DI/AAAAAAAAJBo/COMlZhf9ZG4hLOfr0DpRsDUPqnyCG4DzQCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/E714_Samsung_QuickMeasure_v01.gif\" imageanchor=\"1\" ><img border=\"0\" data-original-width=\"310\" data-original-height=\"675\" /></a></center><p id=\"imgCaption\">Accurately measure with Quick Measure</p><p>To learn more and get started with the ARCore Depth API, get the<a href=\"https://developers.google.com/ar/develop/downloads\"> SDK</a> and visit the <a href=\"https://developers.google.com/ar/whatsnew-arcore\">ARCore developer website</a>. </p><img 08:46:09","updatedTime":"2020-08-25 08:46:09","title":"Building G Suite Add-ons with your favorite tech stack ","link":"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/GDBcode/~3/po04OFR_b44/building-g-suite-add-ons-with-your-favorite-tech-stack.html","description":"<meta name=\"twitter:image\" content=\"https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-woNLs9iCd58/Xz6pdl-1JHI/AAAAAAAAJRE/JGfOlTEoIVklD7kMaYr4Hx2JohaDqr9BQCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/Untitled%2Bdesign%2B%25284%2529.png\"><img style=\"display:none\" src=\"https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-woNLs9iCd58/Xz6pdl-1JHI/AAAAAAAAJRE/JGfOlTEoIVklD7kMaYr4Hx2JohaDqr9BQCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/Untitled%2Bdesign%2B%25284%2529.png\"> <p><em>Posted by Jon Harmer, Product Manager and Steven Bazyl, Developer Advocate for G Suite</em><p><p>Let’s talk about the basics of G Suite Add-ons. G Suite Add-ons simplify how users get things done in G Suite by bringing in functionality from other applications where you need them. They provide a persistent sidebar for quick access, and they are context-aware -- meaning they can react to what you’re doing in context. For example, a CRM add-on can automatically surface details about a sales opportunity in response to an email based on the recipients or even the contents of the message itself.  </p><p>Up until recently, G Suite Add-ons leaned on Apps Script to build Add-ons, but choice is always a good thing, and in some cases you may want to use another scripting language.. So let’s talk about how to build Add-ons using additional runtimes:  </p><p>First, additional runtimes don't add any new capabilities to what you can build. What it does give you is more choice and flexibility in how you build Add-ons. We’ve heard feedback from developers that they would also like the option to use the tools and ecosystems they’ve already learned and invested in. And while there have always been ways to bridge Apps Script and other backends that expose APIs over HTTP/S, it isn't the cleanest of workarounds. .  </p><p><strong>So let’s look at a side by side comparison</strong> of what it looks like to build an Add-on with alternate runtimes:  </p>   <pre class=\"prettyprint\">function homePage() {<br />  let card = CardService.newCardBuilder()<br />    .addSection(CardService.newCardSection()<br />      .addWidget(CardService.newTextParagraph()<br />        .setText(\"Hello world\"))<br />    ).build();<br />  return [card];<br />}</pre>  <p>Here’s the hello world equivalent of an Add-on in Apps Script. Since Apps Script is more akin to a serverless framework like GCF, the code is straightforward -- a function that takes an event and returns the UI to render. </p>   <pre class=\"prettyprint\">// Hello world Node.js<br />const express = require('express');<br />const app = express();<br />app.use(express.json());<br /><br />app.post('/home', (req, res) => {<br />  let card = {<br />    sections: [{<br />      widgets: [{<br />        textParagraph: {<br />          text: 'Hello world'<br />        }<br />      }]<br />    }]<br />  };<br />  res.json({<br />    action: {<br />      navigations: [{<br />        pushCard:  card<br />      }]<br />    }<br />  });<br />}</pre>  <p>This is the equivalent in NodeJS using express, a popular web server framework. It shows a little bit more of the underlying mechanics -- working with the HTTP request/response directly, starting the server, and so on. </p><p>The biggest difference is the card markup -- instead of using CardService, which under the covers builds a protobuf, we're using the JSON representation of the same thing.  </p><pre class=\"prettyprint\">function getCurrentMessage(event) {<br />  var accessToken = event.messageMetadata.accessToken;<br />  var messageId = event.messageMetadata.messageId;<br />  GmailApp.setCurrentMessageAccessToken(accessToken);<br />  return GmailApp.getMessageById(messageId);<br />}<br /></pre><p>Another area where things differ is accessing Google APis. In Apps Script, the clients are available in the global context -- the APIs mostly 'just work'.  Moving to Node requires a little more effort, but not much. </p><p>Apps Script is super easy here. In fact, normally we wouldn't bother with setting the token when using more permissive scopes as it's done for us by Apps Script. We're doing it here to take advantage of the per-message scope that the add-on framework provides. </p><pre class=\"prettyprint\">const { google } = require('googleapis');<br />const { OAuth2Client } = require('google-auth-library');<br />const gmail  = google.gmail({ version: 'v1' });<br /><br />async function fetchMessage(event) {<br />    const accessToken = event.gmail.accessToken;<br />    const auth = new OAuth2Client();<br />    auth.setCredentials({access_token: accessToken});<br /><br />    const messageId = event.gmail.messageId;<br />    const res = await gmail.users.messages.get({<br />        id: messageId,<br />        userId: 'me',<br />        headers: { 'X-Goog-Gmail-Access-Token': event.gmail.accessToken },<br />        auth<br />    });<br />    return res.data;<br />}<br /></pre><p>The NodeJS version is very similar -- a little extra code to import the libraries, but otherwise the same -- extract the message ID and token from the request, set the credentials, then call the API to get the message contents. </p><p><h2>Your Add-on, Your way</h2></p><p>One of the biggest wins for alternate runtimes is the testability that comes with  using your favorite IDE, language, and framework--all of which helps you make developing add-ons more approachable.  </p><p>Both Apps Script and alternate runtimes for G Suite Add-ons have important places in building Add-ons. If you’re getting into building Add-ons or if you want to prototype more complex ones, Apps Script is a good choice.. If you write and maintain systems as your full time job, though, alternate runtimes allow you to use those tools to build your Add-on, letting you leverage work, code and processes that you’re already using. With alternate runtimes for G Suite Add-ons, we want to make it possible for you to extend G Suite in a way that fits your needs using whatever tools you're most comfortable with. </p><p>And don't just take our word for it, hear from one of our early access partners. Shailesh Matariya, CTO at Gfacility has this to say about alternate runtimes: \"We're really happy to use alternate runtimes in G Suite Add-ons. The results have been great and it's much easier to maintain the code. Historically, it would take 4-5 seconds to load data in our Add-on, whereas with alternate runtimes it's closer to 1 second, and that time and efficiency really adds up. Not to mention performance, we're seeing about a 50% performance increase and thanks to this our users are able to manage their workflows with just a few clicks, without having to jump to another system and deal with the hassle of constant updates.\" </p><p><h2>Next Steps</h2></p><p>Read the <a href=\"https://developers.google.com/gsuite/add-ons/guides/alternate-runtimes-overview\">developer documentation</a> for Alternate Runtimes and sign up for the <a href=\"https://docs.google.com/forms/d/e/1FAIpQLSfK8Tv9VinvMhI_navvsjLbNTcmFr1Xr-bbK3iYVRaZI85IiQ/viewform\">early access program</a>.  </p><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/GDBcode/~4/po04OFR_b44\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\"/>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Thu, 20 Aug 2020 16:50:00 href=\"http://coral.ai\">Coral Team</a></em><p> <a href=\"https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-7hpTQLwV7FY/XxdLMJ-YUbI/AAAAAAAAJKc/pD8jCobVq4Ao31abPxEh3Lza1Q5zM642QCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/Coral_Summer_2020_v3.png\" data-original-width=\"1600\" data-original-height=\"1043\" /></a><p>Summer has arrived along with a number of Coral updates. We're happy to announce a new partnership with balena that helps customers build, manage, and deploy IoT applications at scale on Coral devices. In addition, we've released a series of updates to expand platform compatibility, make development easier, and improve the ML capabilities of our devices. </p><p><h3>Open-source Edge TPU runtime now available on GitHub</h3></p><p>First up, our Edge TPU runtime is now open-source and <a href=\"https://github.com/google-coral/libedgetpu\">available on GitHub</a>, including scripts and instructions for building the library for Linux and Windows. Customers running a platform that is not officially supported by Coral, including ARMv7 and RISC-V can now compile the Edge TPU runtime themselves and start experimenting. An open source runtime is easier to integrate into your customized build pipeline, enabling support for creating Yocto-based images as well as other distributions. </p><p><h3>Windows drivers now available for the Mini PCIe and M.2 accelerators</h3></p><p>Coral customers can now also use the <a href=\"https://coral.ai/docs/m2/get-started#2b-on-windows\">Mini PCIe and M.2 accelerators on the Microsoft Windows platform</a>. New Windows drivers for these products complement the previously released Windows drivers for the USB accelerator and make it possible to start prototyping with the <a href=\"https://coral.ai/docs/accelerator/get-started#1c-on-windows\">Coral USB Accelerator on Windows</a> and then to move into production with our Mini PCIe and M.2 products. </p><p><h3>New fresh bits on the Coral ML software stack</h3></p><p>We’ve also made a number of new updates to our ML tools: </p>\n    <ul> \n     <li>The Edge TPU compiler is now version 14.1. It can be updated by running <code>sudo apt-get update &amp;&amp; sudo apt-get install edgetpu</code>, or follow the <a href=\"https://coral.ai/software/#debian-packages\">instructions here</a> <li>Our new Model Pipelining API allows you to divide your model across multiple Edge TPUs. The C++ version is currently in beta and the source is <a href=\"https://github.com/google-coral/edgetpu/tree/master/src/cpp/pipeline\">on GitHub</a> <li>New <a href=\"https://coral.ai/models/#on-device-retraining-classification\">embedding extractor models</a> for EfficientNet, for use with <a href=\"https://coral.ai/docs/edgetpu/retrain-classification-ondevice-backprop/\">on-device backpropagation</a>. Embedding extractor models are compiled with the last fully-connected layer removed, allowing you to retrain for classification. Previously, only Inception and MobileNet were available and now retraining can also be done on EfficientNet <li>New Colab notebooks to <a href=\"https://colab.sandbox.google.com/github/google-coral/tutorials/blob/master/retrain_classification_ptq_tf2.ipynb\">retrain a classification model with TensorFlow 2.0</a> and <a href=\"https://github.com/google-coral/tutorials\">build C++ examples</a></li></li></li></li>\n    </ul><p><h3>Balena partners with Coral to enable AI at the edge</h3></p><p>We are excited to share that the Balena fleet management platform now supports Coral products! </p><p>Companies running a fleet of ML-enabled devices on the edge need to keep their systems up-to-date with the latest security patches in order to protect data, model IP and hardware from being compromised. Additionally, ML applications benefit from being consistently retrained to recognize new use cases with maximum accuracy. Coral + balena together, bring simplicity and ease to the provisioning, deployment, updating, and monitoring of your ML project at the edge, moving early prototyping seamlessly towards production environments with many thousands of devices. </p><p><a href=\"https://www.balena.io/blog/balena-partners-with-coral-to-enable-ai-at-the-edge/\">Read more</a> about all the benefits of Coral devices combined with balena container technology or get started deploying container images to your Coral fleet with this <a href=\"https://github.com/balena-io-examples/coral-streaming-object-detector\">demo project</a>. </p><p><h3>New version of Mendel Linux</h3></p><p><a href=\"https://coral.ai/software/#mendel-linux\">Mendel Linux</a> (5.0 release Eagle) is now available for the Coral Dev Board and SoM and includes a more stable package repository that provides a smoother updating experience. It also brings compatibility improvements and a new version of the GPU driver. </p><p><h3>New models</h3></p><p>Last but not least, we’ve recently released BodyPix, a Google person-segmentation <a href=\"https://blog.tensorflow.org/2019/11/updated-bodypix-2.html\">model</a> that was previously only available for TensorFlow.JS, as a <a href=\"https://github.com/google-coral/project-bodypix\">Coral model</a>. This enables real-time privacy preserving understanding of where people (and body parts) are on a camera frame. We first demoed this at CES 2020 and it was one of our most popular demos. Using BodyPix we can remove people from the frame, display only their outline, and aggregate over time to see heat maps of population flow. </p>\n    <div id=\"flexParent\">\n     <a href=\"https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-rFkCjXuhHHY/XxdM5iQ1W8I/AAAAAAAAJKk/2GR4m3KHB10rsw3vT4WNyHAhrrcpcxpKACLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/gif1.gif\" imageanchor=\"1\"><img border=\"0\" id=\"flexImg\" src=\"https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-rFkCjXuhHHY/XxdM5iQ1W8I/AAAAAAAAJKk/2GR4m3KHB10rsw3vT4WNyHAhrrcpcxpKACLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/gif1.gif\" data-original-width=\"512\" data-original-height=\"288\" /></a>\n     <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-2JSd2PgT2vc/XxdM-yhbzfI/AAAAAAAAJKo/72OuU4KSM085ODUqFqJwlXK1u3r6KCkvwCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/gif2.gif\" imageanchor=\"1\"><img border=\"0\" id=\"flexImg\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-2JSd2PgT2vc/XxdM-yhbzfI/AAAAAAAAJKo/72OuU4KSM085ODUqFqJwlXK1u3r6KCkvwCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/gif2.gif\" data-original-width=\"512\" data-original-height=\"288\" /></a>\n    </div><p id=\"imgCaption\">Here are two possible applications of BodyPix: Body-part segmentation and anonymous population flow. Both are running on the Dev Board.</p><p>We’re excited to add BodyPix to the portfolio of projects the community is using to extend our models far beyond our demos—including tackling today’s biggest challenges. For example, Neuralet has taken our MobileNet V2 SSD Detection model and used it to implement <a href=\"https://neuralet.com/docs/tutorials/smart-social-distancing/\">Smart Social Distancing</a>. Using the bounding box of person detection, they can compute a region for safe distancing and let a user know if social distance isn’t being maintained. The best part is this is done without any sort of facial recognition or tracking, with Coral we can accomplish this in real-time in a privacy preserving manner. </p><p>We can’t wait to see more projects that the community can make with BodyPix. Beyond anonymous population flow there’s endless possibilities with background and body part manipulation. Let us know what you come up with at our <a href=\"https://coral.ai/support\">community channels</a>, including GitHub and StackOverflow. </p><p>\n     <center>\n      ________________________\n     </center></p><p>We are excited to share all that Coral has to offer as we continue to evolve our platform. Developers","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-7hpTQLwV7FY/XxdLMJ-YUbI/AAAAAAAAJKc/pD8jCobVq4Ao31abPxEh3Lza1Q5zM642QCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/Coral_Summer_2020_v3.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx32/cdn21@2020_2/2020/08/25/00-46-10-015_d5c54ef3be811da0.webp","https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-rFkCjXuhHHY/XxdM5iQ1W8I/AAAAAAAAJKk/2GR4m3KHB10rsw3vT4WNyHAhrrcpcxpKACLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/gif1.gif":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx5oss/cdn18@2020_6/2020/08/25/00-46-37-622_450ed7656fac490d.webp","https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-2JSd2PgT2vc/XxdM-yhbzfI/AAAAAAAAJKo/72OuU4KSM085ODUqFqJwlXK1u3r6KCkvwCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/gif2.gif":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx12/cdn74@2020_6/2020/08/25/00-46-37-034_051e16de6ac0a71e.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/GDBcode/~4/7Si33axai8c":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx32/cdn57@2020_6/2020/08/25/00-46-37-263_c93bda8423fad396.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1598316369791},{"createdTime":"2020-08-25 08:46:09","updatedTime":"2020-08-25 08:46:09","title":" Digital Ink Recognition in ML Kit","link":"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/GDBcode/~3/dBFkmH-bawk/digital-ink-recognition-in-ml-kit.html","description":"<meta name=\"twitter:image\" content=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-48oAveGVpcA/Xys1NiyAbVI/AAAAAAAAJN4/nv4b6Xeg8hI8AOBoVBX1HIkqShbYnU1cwCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/digitalink.png\"><img style=\"display:none\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-48oAveGVpcA/Xys1NiyAbVI/AAAAAAAAJN4/nv4b6Xeg8hI8AOBoVBX1HIkqShbYnU1cwCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/digitalink.png\"> <p><em>Posted by Mircea Trăichioiu, Software Engineer, Handwriting Recognition</em><p><a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-48oAveGVpcA/Xys1NiyAbVI/AAAAAAAAJN4/nv4b6Xeg8hI8AOBoVBX1HIkqShbYnU1cwCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/digitalink.png\" imageanchor=\"1\" ><img id=\"imgFull\" border=\"0\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-48oAveGVpcA/Xys1NiyAbVI/AAAAAAAAJN4/nv4b6Xeg8hI8AOBoVBX1HIkqShbYnU1cwCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/digitalink.png\" data-original-width=\"512\" data-original-height=\"218\" /></a><p>A month ago, we announced <a href=\"https://android-developers.googleblog.com/2020/06/mlkit-on-device-machine-learning-solutions.html\">changes to ML Kit to make mobile development with machine learning even easier</a>. Today we're announcing the addition of the <a href=\"https://developers.google.com/ml-kit/vision/digital-ink-recognition/\">Digital Ink Recognition API</a> on both <a href=\"https://developers.google.com/ml-kit/vision/digital-ink-recognition/android\">Android</a> and <a href=\"https://developers.google.com/ml-kit/vision/digital-ink-recognition/ios\">iOS</a> to allow developers to create apps where stylus and touch act as first class inputs. </p><a href=\"https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-qD5pV_AqmBk/Xys1gNiaUNI/AAAAAAAAJOA/yJMzWZv-X-QJGRB32acX-Qt4vUFH2WUxgCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/recognition.png\" imageanchor=\"1\" ><img border=\"0\" src=\"https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-qD5pV_AqmBk/Xys1gNiaUNI/AAAAAAAAJOA/yJMzWZv-X-QJGRB32acX-Qt4vUFH2WUxgCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/recognition.png\" data-original-width=\"1600\" data-original-height=\"533\" /></a><p id=\"imgCaption\">Digital ink recognition: the latest addition to ML Kit’s APIs</p><p>Digital Ink Recognition is different from the existing Vision and Natural Language APIs in ML Kit, as it takes neither text nor images as input. Instead, it looks at the user's strokes on the screen and recognizes what they are writing or drawing. This is the same technology that powers handwriting recognition in Gboard - Google’s own keyboard app, which we described in detail in <a href=\"https://ai.googleblog.com/2019/03/rnn-based-handwriting-recognition-in.html\">a 2019 blog post</a>. It's also the same underlying technology used in the <a href=\"https://quickdraw.withgoogle.com/\">Quick, Draw!</a> and <a href=\"https://experiments.withgoogle.com/autodraw\">AutoDraw</a> experiments. </p> <center><a href=\"https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-gAUAWJrlumM/Xys3HTHMUPI/AAAAAAAAJOM/5OpUf_46jqQMYQWg2swfh4b3yOE9I6-0QCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/handwritingdemo.gif\" imageanchor=\"1\" ><img border=\"0\" src=\"https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-gAUAWJrlumM/Xys3HTHMUPI/AAAAAAAAJOM/5OpUf_46jqQMYQWg2swfh4b3yOE9I6-0QCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/handwritingdemo.gif\" data-original-width=\"288\" data-original-height=\"342\" /></a></center><p id=\"imgCaption\">Handwriting input in Gboard</p> <center><a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-I4dWNhsyuDw/Xys3PJ2LVdI/AAAAAAAAJOQ/jzL0D5DMmxkHz1xOQ-mpPhfraC3JakkqgCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/autodraw.gif\" imageanchor=\"1\" ><img border=\"0\" style=\"width:75%\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-I4dWNhsyuDw/Xys3PJ2LVdI/AAAAAAAAJOQ/jzL0D5DMmxkHz1xOQ-mpPhfraC3JakkqgCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/autodraw.gif\" data-original-width=\"1103\" data-original-height=\"589\" /></a></center><p id=\"imgCaption\">Turning doodles into art with Autodraw</p>  <p>With the new Digital Ink Recognition API, developers can now use this technology in their apps as well, for everything from letting users input text and figures with a finger or stylus to transcribing handwritten notes to make them searchable; all in near real time and entirely on-device. </p><p><h3>Supports many languages and character sets</h3></p><p>Digital Ink Recognition supports <a href=\"https://developers.google.com/ml-kit/vision/digital-ink-recognition/base-models\">300+ languages and 25+ writing systems</a> including all major Latin languages, as well as Chinese, Japanese, Korean, Arabic, Cyrillic, and more. Classifiers parse written text into a string of characters </p><p><h3>Recognizes shapes</h3></p><p>Other classifiers can describe <a href=\"https://developers.google.com/ml-kit/vision/digital-ink-recognition/base-models#shape_classifiers\">shapes</a>, such as drawings and emojis, by the class to which they belong (circle, square, happy face, etc). We currently support an autodraw sketch recognizer, an emoji recognizer, and a basic shape recognizer. </p><p><h3>Works offline</h3></p><p>Digital Ink Recognition API runs on-device and does not require a network connection. However, you must download one or more models before you can use a recognizer. Models are downloaded on demand and are around 20MB in size. Refer to the <a href=\"https://developers.google.com/ml-kit/vision/digital-ink-recognition/android#managing_model_downloads\">model download documentation</a> for more information. </p><p><h3>Runs fast</h3></p><p>The time to perform a recognition call depends on the exact device and the size of the input stroke sequence.  On a typical mobile device recognizing a line of text takes about 100 ms.   </p><p><h3>How to get started</h3></p><p>If you would like to start using Digital Ink Recognition in your mobile app, head over to the <a href=\"https://developers.google.com/ml-kit/vision/digital-ink-recognition\">documentation</a> or check out the sample apps for <a href=\"https://github.com/googlesamples/mlkit/tree/master/android/digitalink\">Android</a> and <a href=\"https://github.com/googlesamples/mlkit/tree/master/ios/quickstarts/digitalinkrecognition\">iOS</a> to see the API in action. For questions or feedback, please reach out to us through one of our <a href=\"https://developers.google.com/ml-kit/community\">community channels</a>. </p><img /></a><h2>Google Pay plugin for Magento 2</h2><p>We are pleased to announce the launch of the official <a href=\"https://goo.gle/GooglePay-Magento-Plugin\">Google Pay plugin for Magento 2</a>. The Google Pay plugin can help increase conversions by enabling a simpler and more secure checkout experience in your Magento website. When you integrate with Google Pay, your customers can complete their purchases quickly using the payment methods they’ve securely saved to their Google Accounts. </p><a href=\"https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-mGBIzJGr80I/Xwij1a7Q_TI/AAAAAAAAJIw/b2wfKV_daPAi6vSTQn7htUVHtsBUF3KSACLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/Magento%2BPlugin%2BPurchase.gif\" imageanchor=\"1\" ><img border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"810\" /></a><p id=\"imgCaption\">Google Pay in action.</p><p>The Google Pay plugin is built in collaboration with Unbound Commerce, is free to use, and integrates with popular payment service providers including Adyen, BlueSnap, Braintree, FirstData - Payeezy & Ucom, Moneris, Stripe, and Vantiv. </p><h2>Installation</h2><p>The Google Pay plugin can be installed from the <a href=\"https://marketplace.magento.com/extensions.html\">Magento Marketplace</a> using this <a href=\"https://goo.gle/GooglePay-Magento-Plugin\">link</a> or by searching the Magento Marketplace for “Google Pay”. </p><p>Refer to the <a href=\"https://docs.magento.com/m2/ee/user_guide/magento/magento-marketplace.html\">Magento Marketplace User Guide</a> for more installation instructions. </p><h2>Getting started</h2><p>To get started with the Google Pay plugin, you will need your Google Pay merchant identifier which can be found in the <a href=\"https://pay.google.com/business/console?utm_source=google_dev_blog&utm_medium=article&utm_campaign=business_console_launch\">Google Pay Business Console</a>. </p><a href=\"https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-74ycnoEHrLM/XwilrXz4GZI/AAAAAAAAJJA/3VvOwLVmtl88N15KEb6kOBw7u1ftDQMqQCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/Integrations%2Bscreen%2B%25E2%2580%2593%2Bmerchant%2Bid%2Bcut%2B1.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" ><img border=\"0\" src=\"https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-74ycnoEHrLM/XwilrXz4GZI/AAAAAAAAJJA/3VvOwLVmtl88N15KEb6kOBw7u1ftDQMqQCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/Integrations%2Bscreen%2B%25E2%2580%2593%2Bmerchant%2Bid%2Bcut%2B1.jpg\" data-original-width=\"1440\" data-original-height=\"1024\" /></a><p id=\"imgCaption\">Your Merchant ID can be found in the Google Pay Business Console.</p><h2>Configuring the Google Pay plugin</h2><p>Once installed, you can configure the plugin in your site’s Magento administration console by navigating to Stores > Configuration > Sales > Payment Methods and selecting the Configure button next to Google Pay.</p><a href=\"https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-R381iSQqttk/Xwil6Cz6ZSI/AAAAAAAAJJE/U3dxIKunrUkN4PTt3VjurpzOQQNlNv44ACLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/configuration.png\" imageanchor=\"1\" ><img border=\"0\" src=\"https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-R381iSQqttk/Xwil6Cz6ZSI/AAAAAAAAJJE/U3dxIKunrUkN4PTt3VjurpzOQQNlNv44ACLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/configuration.png\" data-original-width=\"610\" data-original-height=\"407\" /></a><p id=\"imgCaption\">Click on the Configure button to start the setup process.</p><p>Testing out Google Pay can be achieved in three easy steps: </p><ol> <li>Google Pay credentials: enter your Google Pay merchant ID (available from the <a href=\"https://pay.google.com/business/console?utm_source=google_dev_blog&utm_medium=article&utm_campaign=business_console_launch\">Google Pay Business Console</a>) and merchant name.  <li>Payment gateway credentials: select your payment gateway from the list of payment gateways supported by the Google Pay plugin.  <ol>  <li>Choose the Sandbox environment for testing purposes.   <li>Enter your payment gateway’s credentials into their respective form fields. </li>  </ol> <li>Google Pay settings: enable Google Pay and choose the card networks that you would like to accept. </li></ol><p>You can optionally try out some of the advanced settings that provide the ability to customize the color and type of Google Pay button as well as enabling Minicart integration, which is recommended. </p><a href=\"https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-4G8Q58yVO1I/XwzNWq9BteI/AAAAAAAAJJw/0RlkTxbNqyQ_tIvEaBd2aPttYvh7M7rygCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/advancedsettings.png\" imageanchor=\"1\" ><img border=\"0\" src=\"https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-4G8Q58yVO1I/XwzNWq9BteI/AAAAAAAAJJw/0RlkTxbNqyQ_tIvEaBd2aPttYvh7M7rygCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/advancedsettings.png\" data-original-width=\"1600\" data-original-height=\"1118\" /></a><p id=\"imgCaption\">Checkout the Advanced Settings to further customize how and where the Google Pay button is presented in your store.</p><p>If your payment provider isn’t listed as an option in the payment gateway list, check to see if your payment provider’s plugin has built-in support for Google Pay.</p><h2>Launching Google Pay for your website</h2><p>When you’ve completed your testing, submit your website integration in the <a href=\"https://pay.google.com/business/console?utm_source=google_dev_blog&utm_medium=article&utm_campaign=business_console_launch\">Google Pay Business Console</a>. You will need to provide your website’s URL and screenshots to complete the submission. </p><h2>Summing it up</h2><p>Integrating Google Pay into your website is a great way to increase conversions and to improve the purchasing experience for your customers. </p><p>Find out more about <a href=\"https://pay.google.com/about/business/\">Google Pay</a> and the <a href=\"https://goo.gle/GooglePay-Magento-Plugin\">Google Pay plugin for Magento</a>. </p><h3>What do you think?</h3><p>Do you have any questions? These metrics help you quantify the health and usage of your Action, and gain insight into how users engage with your Action. You can view: </p><ul><li>Execution types and device traits used <li>Daily users and request counts <li>User query response latency <li>Success rate for Smart Home engagements <li>Comparison of cloud and local fulfilment interactions </li></ul><a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-I4ocNvMtIdU/Xvo3Bh-_UMI/AAAAAAAAJC8/8P3kgEqFrrgC_UHg93IHwTFSAKMFtkTXACLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/SmartHomeSuccessDashboard.png\" imageanchor=\"1\" ><img border=\"0\" id=\"imgFull\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-I4ocNvMtIdU/Xvo3Bh-_UMI/AAAAAAAAJC8/8P3kgEqFrrgC_UHg93IHwTFSAKMFtkTXACLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/SmartHomeSuccessDashboard.png\" data-original-width=\"508\" data-original-height=\"297\" /></a><p id=\"imgCaption\">Successful Requests Dashboard</p><p><a href=\"https://cloud.google.com/logging\">Cloud Logging</a> provides detailed logs based on the events observed in Cloud Monitoring.  </p><p>We've added additional features to the error logs to help you quickly debug why intents fail, which particular device commands malfunction, or if your local fulfilment falls back to cloud fulfilment.  </p><p>New details added to the event logs include: </p><ul> <li>Cloud vs. local fulfilment  <li>EXECUTE vs. QUERY intents  <li>Locale of request  <li>Device Type </li></ul><p>You can additionally export these logs through <a href=\"https://cloud.google.com/pubsub\">Cloud Pub/Sub</a>, and build <a href=\"https://cloud.google.com/logging/docs/logs-based-metrics/counter-metrics\">log-based metrics</a> and alerts for your development teams to gain insights into common issues.  </p><p>For more guidance on accessing your Smart Home Action analytics and logs, check out the <a href=\"http://developers.google.com/assistant/smarthome/develop/monitoring-logging\">developer guide</a> or watch the <a href=\"https://youtu.be/NMKTeLJeurA\">video</a>.  </p><p>We want to hear from you! 08:46:09","updatedTime":"2020-08-25 08:46:09","title":" New user features and developer tools to build the helpful home ","link":"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/GDBcode/~3/3iEyH5DtBuA/new-user-features-and-developer-tools-build-helpful-home.html","description":"<meta name=\"twitter:image\" content=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-XMXoklSvnaI/XwXyJkHZ_aI/AAAAAAAAJGo/k5GCs4ezVzo_0GFg4RNwBzLK8QRYGubVgCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/deviceaccess.png\"><img style=\"display:none\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-XMXoklSvnaI/XwXyJkHZ_aI/AAAAAAAAJGo/k5GCs4ezVzo_0GFg4RNwBzLK8QRYGubVgCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/deviceaccess.png\"> <p><em>Posted by Michele Turner, Director of Product and Smart Home Ecosystem for Google Nest</em><p><p>To create a helpful home experience, we have focused on foundational features necessary to make it easier for people to manage their smart devices. But as people spend more and more time at home during these challenging times, it’s important that we invest in additional ways to work with developers to build a more useful connected home.  </p><p>Today, at the <a href=\"https://eventsonair.withgoogle.com/events/heyg-smart-home-summit#\">\"Hey Google\" Smart Home Virtual Summit</a>, we gave updates on our latest smart home initiatives, talked more in-depth about the new smart home controls in Android 11, and previewed some platform tools that we're investing in to make devices easier to set up and work with Google Assistant.  </p><h2>Smart Home for Entertainment Device support with Google Assistant</h2>  <p>As many of us continue to stay home, smart devices are being used a lot more. With the biggest growth coming from entertainment devices, we’re increasing our support in this area with our Smart Home API.  </p><p>Last year, we launched Google Assistant support for <a href=\"https://developers.googleblog.com/2020/07/announcing-new-smart-home-shed-types-and-traits.html\">Smart Home for Entertainment Device (SHED)</a> device types and traits, including TVs, remotes, set-top boxes, speakers, soundbars, and even game consoles from top brands like Xbox, Roku, Dish, and LG. And now, we are making these APIs public for any Smart TV, set-top box or game developers to use. SHED gives users the ability to control their favorite entertainment devices from any Assistant-enabled smart display, smart speaker or mobile device.  </p><h2>Smart Home controls in Android 11 </h2><a href=\"https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-l8hH-uSCmqU/XwXyYFEz_kI/AAAAAAAAJGs/yzXAANQnkC8KzsWFWQaaDjGSws0HtY9yQCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/smarthomecontrols.png\" imageanchor=\"1\" ><img border=\"0\" style=\"width:200px\" id=\"floatRight\" src=\"https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-l8hH-uSCmqU/XwXyYFEz_kI/AAAAAAAAJGs/yzXAANQnkC8KzsWFWQaaDjGSws0HtY9yQCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/smarthomecontrols.png\" data-original-width=\"450\" data-original-height=\"940\" /></a><p>With the release of Android 11, coming out later this year, we are introducing a dedicated space for Smart Home controls that users can find quickly, and access any time. We’ve redesigned the power menu to make devices linked to Google Assistant just a button-press away.   </p><p>Users with the Home App can choose all, or just their favorite controls to be in the space. For partners, you get this for free - there’s no new development work required. We’ll have sliders which will allow you to adjust specific settings, like the temperature of your thermostat in the morning, or how far to open the blinds. You can also customize what devices are visible from the control space and whether these devices can be accessible in your lockscreen.   </p><h2>Improved state reporting and reliability</h2>  <p>With Android 11, we want to give users a quick and easy way to check or adjust the devices in their home. And as we continue to add new surfaces for device control, it becomes more critical to ensure we have accurate state. In the coming months, we’ll be introducing tools to measure your reliability and latency to help improve and debug state reporting. Once you hit key targets for reliability and latency, we will shift from a default of querying your state to using report state to render stateful controls. This will reduce query volume on your servers and improve the user experience with accurate device state across multiple surfaces. </p><p>In addition to state accuracy, the best user experience comes with strong reliability and low latency. To help achieve both, we launched local execution with the <a href=\"https://developers.google.com/assistant/smarthome/concepts/local\">Local Home SDK</a> back in April.  As part of the Smart Home platform, local fulfillment can extend your Smart Home Action and routes commands to devices through the local network, benefitting users with reduced latency and higher reliability by removing an additional cloud hop. </p><p>To ease the development process, the Local Home platform supports both Chrome and Node.js runtime environments, as well as building and testing of apps on local development machines or personal servers. Once you've deployed your local fulfillment app, users will benefit immediately without having to upgrade hardware or manually update firmware. Nanoleaf and Yeelight have already enabled local execution for their devices. It’s available to all developers through the Actions on Google Console.   </p><h2>Improving linking</h2>  <p>Implementing a high quality integration is important - it reduces churn and delights users. Yet, it’s still challenging to get users to discover these features, and we’re doing a couple of things on our end to increase the funnel of users linked to your action. We are excited to launch <a href=\"https://developers.google.com/assistant/smarthome/concepts/account-linking#oauth-based_app_flip\">OAuth-based App Flip</a> on the developer console today. With AppFlip, we streamline the standard account linking flow by flipping users from the Google Home App to the Partner app to gather consent without requiring the users to re-enter their credentials.  </p><p>To increase awareness of your Action, you will soon be able to initiate the account linking flow within your app. There will also be more opportunities to increase awareness through feature promotion and in-app notification using your app, and we will have more details on discovery and linking opportunities later this year.  </p><h2>Robust monitoring, logging, analytics tools</h2>  <p>We know that visibility into the behavior of your smart home integrations is critical, from debugging in early development to detailed analytics in production. To enhance developer productivity, we've integrated with the powerful monitoring and troubleshooting tools available in Google Cloud Platform to provide detailed event logs and usage metrics for smart home projects. </p><p>We’ve also recently <a href=\"https://developers.googleblog.com/2020/06/announcing-enhanced-smart-home-analytics.html\">launched</a> new <a href=\"https://developers.google.com/assistant/smarthome/develop/monitoring-logging\">tools</a> to help developers improve the reliability of their integrations and aid in debugging and resolving issues quickly. You can view aggregate metrics directly in the developer console, or build logs-based metrics to find trends and gain deeper insights into common problems. Google Cloud Platform also enables developers to build custom alerts to quickly identify production issues. </p><p>You can also find a new Smart Home Analytics Dashboard accessible from the developer console and pre-populated with charts for common metrics such as Daily Active Users and Request Breakdown — giving you an overall picture of your integration's behavior. This dashboard is powered by new usage and performance metrics in Google Cloud Monitoring, giving you the power to set alerts and be notified if your integration has an issue. Get started today by going to the “Analytics” tab in the Actions console or the Google Cloud console to check out these new logs, metrics, and alerting capabilities for your projects! </p><h2>Updates to Device Access program </h2>  <p>Last year, we announced that we’re moving from the Works with Nest program to Works with Google Assistant and build on a foundation of <a href=\"https://developers.google.com/nest/device-access\">privacy and data security</a> to ensure users have confidence in how Google and our partners are protecting the consumer’s home data.  </p><p>As part of that effort, we created the <a href=\"https://support.google.com/googlenest/answer/9539279?hl=en\">Device Access</a> program to provide a way for partners to integrate directly with Nest devices. To support the Device Access program, we will soon launch the Device Access Console, a self-serve console that guides commercial developers  through the different project phases: development, certification and pilot testing, and finally production. </p><a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-XMXoklSvnaI/XwXyJkHZ_aI/AAAAAAAAJGo/k5GCs4ezVzo_0GFg4RNwBzLK8QRYGubVgCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/deviceaccess.png\" imageanchor=\"1\" ><img border=\"0\" id=\"imgFull\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-XMXoklSvnaI/XwXyJkHZ_aI/AAAAAAAAJGo/k5GCs4ezVzo_0GFg4RNwBzLK8QRYGubVgCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/deviceaccess.png\" data-original-width=\"1600\" data-original-height=\"771\" /></a><p>For a commercial developer the console allows them to manage your various projects and integrations. It also provides development guides and trait documentation for all supported Nest devices. Individuals who want to create their own automations with their Nest devices will be able to do so with this console, but only for the homes they are a member of. </p><h2>Expanding routines </h2>  <p>One of the most popular features with Nest users is the ability to automatically trigger routines based on whether users are <a href=\"https://support.google.com/googlenest/answer/9251759?hl=en\">Home or Away</a>. Later this year, similar functionality will be available with Google Assistant through occupancy detection.  </p><p>Sleep is also a critical part in maintaining our overall well-being as we stay more at home. Last year we <a href=\"https://blog.google/products/home/spring-healthy-habits-help-google-home/\">launched</a> the <a href=\"https://support.google.com/googlenest/answer/9304145?hl=en#:~:text=The%20Gentle%20Sleep%20and%20Wake,minutes%20to%20imitate%20the%20sunrise.\">Gentle Sleep & Wake feature</a> with Philips Hue, which slowly brightens or dims the lights at a specific time or can be tied to your morning alarms. Just say, “Turn on Gentle Wake up” to your bedroom speaker to ‘set it and forget it.’ The <a href=\"https://developers.google.com/assistant/smarthome/traits/lighteffects\">Light Effects trait</a> is now public so all developers can integrate their native Sleep or Wake experiences - in fact LIFX has recently launched! We encourage you to build and integrate your own unique experiences. We’ll have a larger launch moment later this year when we launch emulated Sleep and Wake effects so that it’ll work out of the box for any smart light!  </p><p>Another way partners will be able to innovate on our platform and provide more helpful experiences to users is by extending personal routines with custom routines designed by partners, available in the coming months. Developers will be able to create and suggest routines, not just for their devices, but that can work with other devices in a customer’s home. You’ll be able to create solutions for your customers that are based on your core business and bring value to your customers - whether it’s wellness, cleaning, or entertainment. Users will be able to browse and opt-in to approved routines and choose to have Nest and other devices react and participate in that routine.  </p><p>Our Smart Home efforts have grown significantly over the past several years. We now have integrations with thousands of partners covering all the major connected product categories and devices, and will continue our ambitious goal to build deeper in-home integrations. Be sure to review our docs/samples/videos to learn about all the cool new stuff, and <a href=\"https://developers.google.com/assistant/community\">connect</a> with us on our dev communities. </p><img content=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-1BpmnMhElkk/XvzLtKaV-zI/AAAAAAAAJDs/YVeXCyyqqEEuDXudtICtR_rYKidYY5lWwCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/SHED_updated.png\"><img style=\"display:none\" Advocate</em><p> <p>Back in April, we released the first set of Smart Home Entertainment Device (SHED) types, including TV, set-top box, and remote, as well as the traits AppSelector, InputSelector, MediaState, TransportControl, and Volume. We are excited to announce the release of new Smart Home Entertainment Device (SHED) types and traits. These new device types and traits compliment the original set we released earlier this year, and help build out a more complete solution for smart home media and gaming devices. By implementing these types and traits on your entertainment devices, you can enable users to fully access device and media controls from any Assistant surface.</p> <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-1BpmnMhElkk/XvzLtKaV-zI/AAAAAAAAJDs/YVeXCyyqqEEuDXudtICtR_rYKidYY5lWwCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/SHED_updated.png\" imageanchor=\"1\" ><img border=\"0\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-1BpmnMhElkk/XvzLtKaV-zI/AAAAAAAAJDs/YVeXCyyqqEEuDXudtICtR_rYKidYY5lWwCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/SHED_updated.png\" data-original-width=\"1182\" data-original-height=\"330\" /></a> <p id=\"imgCaption\">SHED Types and Traits</p> <p>To expand the SHED options, we've released the following new device types for Smart Home: </p><ul> <li>Audio-video receiver  <li>Streaming box  <li>Streaming stick  <li>Soundbar  <li>Streaming soundbar  <li>Speaker </li></ul><p>We've also released the following new trait: </p><ul> <li>Channel </li></ul><p>To ensure a consistent, high-quality experience for all end users, each of these device types require your service to report <code>activityState</code> and <code>playbackState</code> to Google using the ReportState API. This requirement improves the portability between media devices and helps the Assistant better understand user intents for these devices. By implementing the complete set of recommended device traits, you can further improve the quality of your smart home Action and improve device targeting for media playback command fulfilment. </p><p>For more information on how to implement these new device features, check out the <a href=\"https://developers.google.com/assistant/smarthome/concepts/devices-traits\">docs</a> and <a href=\"https://github.com/actions-on-google/smart-home-nodejs\">samples</a>. You can also join us at our \"<a href=\"https://eventsonair.withgoogle.com/events/heyg-smart-home-summit\">Hey Google\" Smart Home Virtual Summit</a> to learn more about these new features.  </p><p>We want to hear from you, so continue sharing your feedback with us through the <a href=\"https://issuetracker.google.com/issues/new?component=655104&template=1284327\">issue tracker</a>, and engage with other smart home developers in the <a href=\"https://www.reddit.com/r/GoogleAssistantDev\">/r/GoogleAssistantDev</a> community. Follow <a href=\"https://twitter.com/ActionsOnGoogle\">@ActionsOnGoogle</a> on Twitter for more of our team's updates, and tweet using #AoGDevs to share what you’re working on. It allows you to take advantage of the flexibility of development while scaling the infrastructure as needed. </p><p>  I'm often asked by developers to provide a list of Google Cloud architectures that help to get started on the cloud journey. Last month, I decided to start a mini-series on Twitter called “#13DaysOfGCP\" where I shared the most common use cases on Google Cloud. I have compiled the list of all 13 architectures in this post. Some of the topics covered are hybrid cloud, mobile app backends, microservices, serverless, CICD and more. apps","link":"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/GDBcode/~3/vEv6btr1JWQ/introducing-cast-connect-android-tv.html","description":"<meta name=\"twitter:image\" content=\"https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-jZnpRo1KHrA/XyyTXFGGlnI/AAAAAAAAJOo/xXueBQl-gaUOI5O8WSbYAHOa0DqG5g1GQCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/Screen%2BShot%2B2020-08-06%2Bat%2B4.33.35%2BPM.png\"><img style=\"display:none\" src=\"https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-jZnpRo1KHrA/XyyTXFGGlnI/AAAAAAAAJOo/xXueBQl-gaUOI5O8WSbYAHOa0DqG5g1GQCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/Screen%2BShot%2B2020-08-06%2Bat%2B4.33.35%2BPM.png\"> <p><em>Posted by Meher Vurimi, Product Manager</em><p><p>For more than seven years, <a href=\"https://developers.google.com/cast/\">Google Cast</a> has made it easy for users to enjoy your content on the big screen with Chromecast or a Chromecast built-in TV. We’re always looking to improve the casting experiences, which is why we’re excited to introduce <a href=\"https://developers.google.com/cast/docs/android_tv_receiver\">Cast Connect</a>. This new feature allows users to cast directly to your Android TV app while still  allowing control from your sender app. </p><p><h2>Why is this helpful?</h2></p><p>With <a href=\"https://developers.google.com/cast?hl=en\">Google Cast</a> your app is the remote control - helping users find, play, pause, seek, stop, and otherwise control what they’re watching. It enables you to extend video or audio from your Android, iOS, or Chrome app to a TV or sound system. With <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/tv\">Android TV</a>, partners are able to build apps that let users experience your app's immersive content on their TV screen and control with a remote.  </p><p>With <a href=\"https://developers.google.com/cast/docs/android_tv_receiver\">Cast Connect</a>, we are combining the best of both worlds; first, by prioritizing playback via the Android TV app to deliver a richer and more immersive experience, and second, by allowing the user to still control their experience from your Android, iOS or Chrome app, and now, also directly using their Android TV’s remote control. Cast Connect helps the user easily engage with other content directly on the TV instead of  only having to use your mobile device to browse for additional content.  </p><a href=\"https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-2ZS4A6rR3e0/XyySUJOuHSI/AAAAAAAAJOg/tifV44XDdkwwfBz7dpyHvQllAxHt_ufLgCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/STAN_CastConnect_v3%2B3.gif\" imageanchor=\"1\" ><img border=\"0\" src=\"https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-2ZS4A6rR3e0/XyySUJOuHSI/AAAAAAAAJOg/tifV44XDdkwwfBz7dpyHvQllAxHt_ufLgCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/STAN_CastConnect_v3%2B3.gif\" data-original-width=\"957\" data-original-height=\"537\" /></a><p id=\"imgCaption\">Cast Connect User Journey on  Stan</p><p><h2>Availability</h2></p><p>We’re working closely with a number of partners on bringing Cast Connect to their Apps and, most recently, we’re excited to announce that <a href=\"https://www.cbs.com/all-access/?gclsrc=aw.ds&ds_rl=1275739&ref=__iv_p_1_g_15527027287_w_kwd-170170805047_h_9032188_ii__d_c_v__n_g_c_247169935667_l__t__e__r__vi__&ftag=AAM03c5ced&vndid=google$null$null$cbs.all%20access&gclid=EAIaIQobChMIpfDwga3L6gIVXx-tBh05RwXGEAAYASAAEgITYfD_BwE&gclsrc=aw.ds&_ivgu=5ed10151-d6e8-4681-b3d6-8b067c2b7fa2\">CBS</a> and our Australian SVOD partner, <a href=\"https://www.stan.com.au/\">Stan</a> have launched Cast Connect. Starting today, the <a href=\"https://developers.google.com/cast/docs/reference/atv_receiver/packages\">Cast Connect library</a> is available on Android, iOS and Chrome. To get started with adding Cast Connect to your existing framework, head over to the <a href=\"https://developers.google.com/cast/docs/android_tv_receiver\">Google Cast Developers</a> site. Along the way, the Cast SDK team and the developer community are available to help you and answer questions on Stack Overflow by using the <i><strong>google-cast-connect</strong></i> tag. </p><p>Happy Developers","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-jZnpRo1KHrA/XyyTXFGGlnI/AAAAAAAAJOo/xXueBQl-gaUOI5O8WSbYAHOa0DqG5g1GQCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/Screen%2BShot%2B2020-08-06%2Bat%2B4.33.35%2BPM.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn73@2020_6/2020/08/25/00-46-10-046_d66aceaa142b32fe.webp","https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-2ZS4A6rR3e0/XyySUJOuHSI/AAAAAAAAJOg/tifV44XDdkwwfBz7dpyHvQllAxHt_ufLgCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/STAN_CastConnect_v3%2B3.gif":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx27/cdn57@2020_6/2020/08/25/00-46-46-067_f282b27e81292a43.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/GDBcode/~4/vEv6btr1JWQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx24/cdn18@2020_1/2020/08/25/00-46-36-740_d1e3b46e71946317.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1598316369790},{"createdTime":"2020-08-25 08:46:09","updatedTime":"2020-08-25 08:46:09","title":" Teaching the art of great documentation","link":"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/GDBcode/~3/NijqnnlYGoM/teaching-art-of-great-documentation.html","description":"<meta name=\"twitter:image\" content=\"https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-psXX_PVSVdg/XwYMQYHTWtI/AAAAAAAAJG4/wKZ0nEbIbyIolSRHMg1g3MAJUMwRjRzTACLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/figure1.png\"><img style=\"display:none\" src=\"https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-psXX_PVSVdg/XwYMQYHTWtI/AAAAAAAAJG4/wKZ0nEbIbyIolSRHMg1g3MAJUMwRjRzTACLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/figure1.png\"> <p><em>Posted by <a href=\"https://twitter.com/scottydocs?lang=en\">James Scott</a>, Technical writer</em><p> <p>Technical writing is simple - you merely have to explain brutally complex technologies to relentlessly unforgiving audiences. It's unsurprising that so many engineers find writing documentation is the most painful part of their job. If you would like to teach your colleagues to become writers, the good news is Google's fun and interactive technical writing course materials are free and available for everyone to use! Alternatively, if you're a developer who would like to learn how to write more clearly, you can read through the course work for yourself or convince a colleague to teach the course at your organisation! </p><p>We researched documentation extensively, and it turns out that the best sentences in the world consist primarily of words. Our self-paced and facilitator-led courses will not only help software engineers choose the right words but also help to make the whole writing process a lot less scary. Perhaps software engineers won't become William Shakespeare or even William Shatner overnight, but hopefully they will gain the confidence to write something worth publishing. As working from home becomes more common, good documentation has never been more important in enabling software engineers to work independently.  </p><h2>Courses overview</h2><p>Google introduced the technical writing courses, Technical Writing One and Technical Writing Two, in 2015. Since then, thousands of Google software engineers and product managers have taken and enjoyed the courses. In February 2020, we released the courses to the world.  </p><p>The classes have the following structure: </p><ul> <li>Students complete self-study work before attending the live class. The self-study work is valuable on its own, even for students who will never attend the live class.  <li>A facilitator guides students through a live class. The live class features practical exercises, class discussion, and extensive peer-to-peer feedback. Note that Google does not lead these live courses but provides extensive material to help facilitators prepare to lead them. </li></ul><p>Organizations can choose to host the live classes virtually or in-person. </p><h2>Technical Writing One</h2><p>The first course, Technical Writing One, covers the basics of technical writing. Students learn to start thinking about their audience before even putting pen to paper. For example, in one exercise, students are challenged to write instructions for putting toothpaste on a toothbrush. That might sound relatively simple, but here's the catch - your audience has never brushed their teeth before. That's not to say they have bad oral hygiene, but they don't even know what a toothbrush is. The exercise aims to get students to think about documenting a completely new technology. </p><p>Another important lesson that Technical Writing One teaches you is how to shorten the sentence length in your documentation and how to edit unnecessarily long sentences. Hopefully once you have taken the course, you might edit the preceding sentence down to something like the following: <del>Another important lesson that</del> <strong>Technical Writing One teaches you </strong><del>is</del> <strong>to shorten sentences <del>length in your documentation and how to edit unnecessarily long sentences</del></strong>.  </p><p>The course also advocates using lists instead of walls of text, so here, in list form, are some other topics it covers: </p><ul> <li>Using active voice instead of passive voice.  <li>Revising text into clear paragraphs.  <li>Learning various self-editing techniques. </li></ul><h2>Technical Writing Two</h2><p>Technical Writing Two builds on the techniques from the first course and is for those who already know verbs from adverbs. The course encourages students to express their creative side. For example, in one exercise, students find the best way to illustrate technical concepts. Spoiler alert: can you spot any issues with the following diagram?</p><a href=\"https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-psXX_PVSVdg/XwYMQYHTWtI/AAAAAAAAJG4/wKZ0nEbIbyIolSRHMg1g3MAJUMwRjRzTACLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/figure1.png\" imageanchor=\"1\" ><img border=\"0\" src=\"https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-psXX_PVSVdg/XwYMQYHTWtI/AAAAAAAAJG4/wKZ0nEbIbyIolSRHMg1g3MAJUMwRjRzTACLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/figure1.png\" data-original-width=\"1600\" data-original-height=\"620\" alt=\"A diagram titled Finding a website through DNS, with seven boxes of varying colour, size, and shape connected by lines in various directions.\" /></a><p id=\"imgCaption\">Figure 1: Finding a website through DNS</p><p>Other intermediate techniques the course covers include: </p><ul> <li>Organizing large doc sets.  <li>Revising and reorganizing text.  <li>Writing accurate descriptions.  <li>Creating tutorials for beginners. </li></ul><p>Students take part in interactive exercises and peer review with a lab partner. Technical Writing Two also includes class discussions on documentation types and how to write the dreaded first draft.  </p><h2>Want to know more?</h2>  <p>If you would like to teach the courses at your own organization, see the <a href=\"https://developers.google.com/tech-writing/for-instructors\">facilitator guides</a>. To review the pre-work and read through the training materials, see the <a href=\"https://developers.google.com/tech-writing/overview\">course overviews</a>.  </p><img Developers","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-2M--vBrMiLs/XvYdIjq503I/AAAAAAAAJCk/jN-tbdFQs5sr_IMvbrK156A8ewxaXvtkgCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/Entertainment%2BBlog%2BHero%2BImage%2B%25281%2529.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx24/cdn86@2020_3/2020/08/25/00-46-09-971_616f3a3581679cc2.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/GDBcode/~4/77qj2quzinU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx5oss/cdn30@2020_5/2020/08/25/00-46-36-943_400b8fff201766bc.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1598316369797},{"createdTime":"2020-08-25 08:46:09","updatedTime":"2020-08-25 08:46:09","title":"Voice Global 2020: New improvements to core platform and development tools for Google Assistant","link":"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/GDBcode/~3/d6rNew0LewU/voice-global-2020-new-improvements-to-core-platform.html","description":"<meta name=\"twitter:image\" content=\"https://3.bp.blogspot.com/--IVuvw89EHs/Xuk9n7rekvI/AAAAAAAAI6Q/bC6HOmMRKuYVPgbsyWK4e3hEFgkdviHDQCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/Actions%2BBuilder%2Bscreenshot%2B1.jpg\"><img style=\"display:none\" src=\"https://3.bp.blogspot.com/--IVuvw89EHs/Xuk9n7rekvI/AAAAAAAAI6Q/bC6HOmMRKuYVPgbsyWK4e3hEFgkdviHDQCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/Actions%2BBuilder%2Bscreenshot%2B1.jpg\"> <p><em>Posted by Payam Shodjai, Director of Product Management, Google Assistant </em><p><p>Today at <a href=\"https://www.voicesummit.ai/global\">VOICE Global</a>, we shared our vision for Google Assistant to truly be the best way to get things done - and the important role that developers play in that vision, especially as voice experiences continue to evolve. </p><p>Google Assistant helps more than 500 million people every month in over 30 languages across 90 countries get things done at home and on the go. What’s at the heart of this growth is the simple insight that people want a more natural way to get what they need. That’s why we’ve invested heavily in making sure Google Assistant works seamlessly across devices and services and offers quick and accurate help.  </p><p>Over the last few months, we’ve seen people’s needs shifting, and this is reflected in how Google Assistant is being used and the role that it can play to help navigate these changes. For example, to help people get accurate information on Search and Maps - like modified store hours or information on pick-up and delivery - we have been using <a href=\"https://www.blog.google/inside-google/company-announcements/covid-19-how-were-continuing-to-help/\">Duplex</a> conversational technology to contact businesses and update over half a million business listings.  </p><p>We’ve also been working with our partners to bring great educational experiences into the home, so that families can continue learning in a communal setting. Bamboo Learning is bringing their voice-forward education platform to Google Assistant, with fun, new ways to learn history, math, and reading. Our <a href=\"https://www.blog.google/products/google-fit/be-healthy-at-home/\">hand-washing songs</a> continue to be popular. The songs leverage WaveNet's natural expressiveness – allowing us to train Google Assistant to sing across numerous generated voices users can pick from.  </p><h2>Building Google Assistant experiences gets easier</h2>  <p>Great experiences are at the core of what makes Google Assistant truly helpful. To help existing and aspiring developers build new experiences with ease, we are making some major improvements to our core platform and development tools. Rather than needing to hop back and forth between <a href=\"https://developers.google.com/assistant/console\">Actions Console</a> and Dialogflow to build an Action, wouldn’t it be great if there were one integrated platform for building on Google Assistant? </p><p>Starting today, we’re releasing <a href=\"https://developers.googleblog.com/2020/06/announcing-actions-builder-actions-sdk.html\">Actions Builder</a>, a new web-based IDE that provides a graphical interface to show the entire conversation flow. It allows you to manage Natural Language Understanding (NLU) training data and provides advanced debugging tools. And, it is fully integrated into the Actions Console so you can now build, debug, test, release, and analyze your Actions - all in one place.  </p><p>If you prefer to  work in your own tools, you can use the updated <a href=\"https://developers.googleblog.com/2020/06/announcing-actions-builder-actions-sdk.html\">Actions SDK</a>. For the first time, you’ll have a file based representation of your action and the ability to use a local IDE. The SDK not only enables local authoring of NLU and conversation schemas, but it also allows bulk import and export of training data to improve conversation quality.  The Actions SDK is accompanied by a command line interface, so you can build and manage an action fully in code using your favorite source control and continuous integration tools. </p><p>With these two releases, we are also introducing a new conversation model and improvements to the runtime engine. Now, it’s easier to design and build conversations and users will get faster and more accurate responses. We’re very excited about this suite of products which replaces Dialogflow as the preferred way to develop conversational actions on Google Assistant. </p><p><a href=\"https://3.bp.blogspot.com/--IVuvw89EHs/Xuk9n7rekvI/AAAAAAAAI6Q/bC6HOmMRKuYVPgbsyWK4e3hEFgkdviHDQCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/Actions%2BBuilder%2Bscreenshot%2B1.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" ><img border=\"0\" src=\"https://3.bp.blogspot.com/--IVuvw89EHs/Xuk9n7rekvI/AAAAAAAAI6Q/bC6HOmMRKuYVPgbsyWK4e3hEFgkdviHDQCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/Actions%2BBuilder%2Bscreenshot%2B1.jpg\" data-original-width=\"1600\" data-original-height=\"996\" /></a></p><h2>New functionality to create interactive voice actions </h2>  <p>Based on feedback from developers, we’re also adding new functionality to build more interactive experience on Google Assistant with Home Storage, updated Media API and Continuous Match Mode.  </p><p>One of the exciting things about speakers and smart displays is that they’re communal. <a href=\"https://developers.google.com/assistant/conversational/storage-home\">Home Storage</a> is a new feature that provides a communal storage solution for devices connected on the home graph and allows developers to save context for all individual users, such as the last saved point from a puzzle game. </p><p>  </p><p><a href=\"https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-ARDnV3HDorc/Xuk9tGLjIDI/AAAAAAAAI6U/w4N8FFNCkUUuGtmT_iUkwsIJO2w-TP5twCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/homeStorage.gif\" imageanchor=\"1\" ><img border=\"0\" src=\"https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-ARDnV3HDorc/Xuk9tGLjIDI/AAAAAAAAI6U/w4N8FFNCkUUuGtmT_iUkwsIJO2w-TP5twCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/homeStorage.gif\" data-original-width=\"722\" data-original-height=\"518\" /></a></p><p>Our updated Media APIs now support longer-form media sessions and lets users resume playback of content across surfaces. For example, users can start playback from a specific moment or resume where  they dropped out of their previous session. </p><p>Sometimes you want to build experiences that enable users to speak more naturally with your action, without waiting for a change in mic states. Rolling out in the next few months, Continuous Match Mode allows Assistant to respond immediately to a user’s speech for more fluid experiences by recognizing defined words and phrases set by you. This is done transparently so that before the mic opens, Assistant will announce the mic will stay open temporarily so users know they can speak freely without waiting for additional prompts. For example, CoolGames is launching a game in a few weeks called, “Guess The Drawing” that uses Continuous Match Mode to allow the user to continuously guess what the drawing is until they get it right. The game is also built with <a href=\"https://developers.google.com/assistant/interactivecanvas\">Interactive Canvas</a> for a more visual and immersive experience on smart displays.  </p><h2>Bringing AMP to smart displays</h2>  <p>In addition to making it easy for you to build new experiences for Google Assistant, we also want to bring the depth of great web content together with the simple and robust <a href=\"https://developers.google.com/amp\">AMP</a> framework to deliver new experiences on Smart Displays. AMP allows you to create compelling, smooth websites that have a great user experience. AMP compliant articles are coming to smart displays later this summer with News. Stay tuned for more updates in the coming months as we expand to enable more web content categories for Smart Displays. </p><p>With these tools, we want to empower developers to build helpful experiences of the future with Google Assistant, enabling people to get what they need more simply, while giving them time back to focus on what matters most. </p><img
