08:46:09","updatedTime":"2020-08-25 08:46:09","title":"Introducing an easier way to design your G Suite Add-on","link":"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/GDBcode/~3/2UtMHzZ17n0/introducing-easier-way-to-design-your-gsuite-add-on.html","description":"<meta name=\"twitter:image\" content=\"https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-KnEqsG7lrcM/Xwd1_onTuyI/AAAAAAAAJHQ/o6yKT__5yDoqPcwuyjj9gP88oW7ar2__wCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/step1.gif\"><img style=\"display:none\" src=\"https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-KnEqsG7lrcM/Xwd1_onTuyI/AAAAAAAAJHQ/o6yKT__5yDoqPcwuyjj9gP88oW7ar2__wCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/step1.gif\"> <p><em>Posted by Kylie Poppen, Senior Interaction Designer, G Suite and Akshay Potnis, Interaction Designer, G Suite</em><p> <p>You’ve just scoped out an awesome new way to solve for your customer’s next challenge, but wait, what about the design? Building an integration between your software platform and another comes with a laundry list of things to think about: your vision, your users, their experience, your partners, APIs, developer docs, and so on. Caught between two different platforms, many constraints, and limited time, you're probably wondering: how might we build the most intuitive and powerful user experience? </p><p>Imagine making a presentation, with Google Slides you have all sorts of templates to get you started, and you can build a great deck easily. But, to build a seamless integration between two software platforms, those pre-built templates don’t exist and you basically have to start from scratch. In the best case scenario, you’d create your own components and layer them on top of each other with the goal of making the UI seem just about right. But this takes time. Hours longer than you want it to. Without design guidelines, you're stuck guessing what is or is not possible, looking to other apps and emulating what they've already done. Which leads us to the reality that some add-ons have a suboptimal experience, because time is limited, and you're left to build only for what you know you can do, rather than what's actually possible.  </p><p>To simplify all of this, we’re introducing the <a href=\"https://www.figma.com/community/file/848275628252039675\">G Suite Add-ons UI Design Kit</a>, now live on Figma. With it you can browse all of the components of G Suite Add-ons’ <a href=\"https://developers.google.com/gsuite/add-ons/concepts/card-interfaces\">card-based interface</a>, learn best practices, and simply drag-and-drop to create your own unique designs. Save the time spent recreating what an add-on will look like, so that you can spend that time thinking about how your add-on will work .  </p><p>While the UI Design Kit has only been live for a little over a month, we’ve already been hearing feedback from our partners about its impact.  </p><p>“Zapier connects more than 2,000 apps, allowing businesses to automate repetitive, time-consuming tasks. When building these integrations, we want to ensure a seamless experience for our customers,” said Ryan Powell, Product Manager at Zapier. “However, a partner’s UI can be difficult to navigate when starting from scratch. G Suite’s UI Design Kit allows us to build, test and optimize integrations because we know from the start what is and is not possible inside of GSuite’s UI.” </p><h2>Here’s how to use the UI Design Kit:</h2><h3>Step 1</h3><p>Find and duplicate design kit </p><ul> <li>Search for G suite on Figma community or use this <a href=\"https://www.figma.com/community/file/848275628252039675\">link</a> <li>Open G Suite Add Ons UI Design Kit  <li>Just click the duplicate button. </li></ul><a & structure. </li></ul><a href=\"https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-nte6fdZqbD4/Xwd27kJljPI/AAAAAAAAJHo/W5xCh_hzrPcdezz-bCnHX3qF7cG4h6fmgCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/step3b.gif\" imageanchor=\"1\" ><img id=\"imgFull\" /></a><h2>Next Steps to Consider:</h2><p>With G Suite Add-ons, users and admins can seamlessly get their work done, across their favorite workplace applications, without needing to leave G Suite. With this UI Design Kit, you too can focus your time on building a great user experience inside of G Suite, while simplifying and accelerating the design process. Follow these steps to get started today:  </p><p><a href=\"https://www.figma.com/community/file/848275628252039675\">Download the UI Design Kit</a></p><p><a href=\"https://developers.google.com/gsuite/add-ons/overview\">Get started with G Suite Add-ons</a></p><p>Hopefully this will inspire you to build more add-ons using the Cards Framework! 08:46:09","updatedTime":"2020-08-25 08:46:09","title":"Discontinuing support for JSON-RPC and global HTTP batch endpoints","link":"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/GDBcode/~3/hHSfS_4jwCs/discontinuing-support-for-json-rpc-and.html","description":"<meta name=\"twitter:image\" content=\"https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-34CQznme--I/WmvQde4mXmI/AAAAAAAAEa8/OEwsdN_w8eIgk79mTxuVk-b1p3uqM0vogCLcBGAs/s1600/Screen%2BShot%2B2018-01-26%2Bat%2B5.03.14%2BPM.png\">\n <p><strong>UPDATE: <p> August 19, 2020: Revised guidance for Google Cloud client libraries and Apache Beam/Cloud Dataflow </p><p>August 12, 2020: Added guidance for Dataproc hadoop connector </p><p>July 13, 2020: Enumerate endpoints for JSON-RPC and Global HTTP Batch. Include examples of Non-Global HTTP Batch endpoints for contrast.</p><p>July 8, 2020: Limit usage of JSON-RPC and Global HTTP batch endpoints to existing projects only. Starting July 15 (JSON-RPC) and July 16 (Global HTTP Batch) we will no longer allow new projects to call these two endpoints. Projects with calls in the last 4 weeks will continue to work until the deadline of Aug 12, 2020.</p><p>Apr 23, 2020: gcloud min version has been updated <p>Apr 22, 2020: error injection planned for Apr 28 is CANCELLED, JSON-RPC and Global HTTP batch endpoint will perform normally. Next error injection window will be on May 26 as scheduled. </p></p></strong></p>\n <p>We have invested heavily in our API and service infrastructure to improve performance and security and to add features developers need to build world-class APIs. As we make changes we must address features that are no longer compatible with the latest architecture and business requirements. </p>\n <p>The JSON-RPC protocol (<a href=\"http://www.jsonrpc.org/specification\">http://www.jsonrpc.org/specification</a>) and Global HTTP Batch (<a href=\"https://developers.google.com/classroom/guides/batch\">example</a>) are two such features. Our support for these features was based on an architecture using a single shared proxy to receive requests for all APIs. As we move towards a more distributed, high performance architecture where requests go directly to the appropriate API server we can no longer support these global endpoints.<a name=\"more\"></a></p>\n <p>We had originally planned to decommission these features by Mar 25, 2019. However, it came to our attention that few highly impacted customers might not have received the earlier notification. </p>\n <p>As a result, we are extending the deprecation timeline to Aug 12, 2020, when we will discontinue support for both these features. Please note the timeline extension to Aug 12, 2020 does not apply to Places API. Please visit <a href=\"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/GDBcode/~3/hHSfS_4jwCs/ https://developers.google.com/places/ios-sdk/client-migration\">Places SDK for iOS migration</a> for information on Places API migration. </p>\n <p>Starting February 2020 and running through August 2020, we will periodically inject errors for short windows of time. Please see below for exact details and schedule of planned downtime windows. </p>\n <p>We know that these changes have customer impact and have worked to make the transition steps as clear as possible. Please see the guidance below which will help ease the transition. </p>\n <h2><strong>Planned downtime</strong></h2> \n <p>To enable customers to identify systems that depend on these deprecated features, before the final turndown date is reached, there will be scheduled downtime for Global Batch and JSON-RPC starting from February 2020 and running through August 2020. </p>\n <p>Below are details and schedule of periodic error injection windows, details of the downtime in June and July will be confirmed nearer the time, so please check back this <a href=\"https://developers.googleblog.com/2018/03/discontinuing-support-for-json-rpc-and.html\">blog post</a> for the latest schedule. </p>\n <a href=\"https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-EniMfDvdDgM/XwSwta5ae8I/AAAAAAAAJF0/vPIPsEWo794_UfXbvvoDeUB9kHFQPam6ACLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/updated.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-EniMfDvdDgM/XwSwta5ae8I/AAAAAAAAJF0/vPIPsEWo794_UfXbvvoDeUB9kHFQPam6ACLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/updated.jpg\" data-original-width=\"1275\" data-original-height=\"1502\" /></a> \n <h2><strong>How do I know if I should migrate ?</strong></h2> \n <h3><strong><span style=\"text-decoration:underline;\">JSON-RPC</span></strong></h3> \n <p>To identify whether you use JSON-RPC, you can check whether you send requests to <code><em>\"https://www.googleapis.com/rpc\"</em></code> or <code><em>\"https://content.googleapis.com/rpc\"</em></code>. If you do, you should migrate. </p>\n <h3><strong><span style=\"text-decoration:underline;\">HTTP batch</span></strong></h3> \n <p>A batch request is homogenous if the inner requests are addressed to the same API, even if addressed to different methods of the same API. Homogenous batching will still be supported but through <em>API specific</em> batch endpoints. If you are currently forming homogeneous batch requests, using <a href=\"https://developers.google.com/api-client-library/\">Google API Client Libraries</a> or using non-Google API client libraries or no client library (i.e making raw HTTP requests), you should migrate. </p>\n <p>A batch request is heterogeneous if the inner requests go to different APIs. Heterogeneous batching will not be supported after the turn down of the Global HTTP batch endpoint. If you are currently forming heterogeneous batch requests, change your client code to send only homogenous batch requests, i.e you should migrate. </p>\n <h2><strong>What do you need to do to migrate ?</strong></h2> \n <p>Clients will need to make the changes outlined below to migrate. </p>\n <h2><strong><span style=\"text-decoration:underline;\">JSON-RPC</span></strong></h2>\n <h2><strong>Endpoints</strong></h2> \n <p>The following JSON-RPC endpoints will no longer be supported. </p>\n <ul> \n  <li><a href=\"https://www.googleapis.com/rpc\">https://www.googleapis.com/rpc</a> <li><a href=\"https://content.googleapis.com/rpc\">https://content.googleapis.com/rpc</a> <li><a href=\"https://clients6.google.com/rpc\">https://clients6.google.com/rpc</a></li></li></li>\n </ul> \n <h2><strong>Using Client Libraries</strong></h2> \n <p> If you are using JSON-RPC client libraries (either the Google published libraries or other libraries), switch to REST client libraries and modify your application to work with REST client libraries. </p>\n <p> <strong>Example code for Javascript<br /></strong> <em>Before</em><br> <pre class=\"prettyprint\">// json-rpc request for the list method<br />gapi.client.rpcRequest('zoo.animals.list', 'v2',<br />  {name:'giraffe'}).execute(x=&gt;console.log(x))<br /></pre> <em>After<br /></em><pre class=\"prettyprint\"><em>// json-rest request for the list method</em><br />gapi.client.zoo.animals.list({name:'giraffe'}).then(x=&gt;console.log(x))<br /></pre> <h2> <strong>Not Using Client Libraries i.e making raw HTTP requests</strong></h2> <p> If you are not using client libraries (i.e. making raw HTTP requests): </p>\n   <ol> \n    <li>Use the REST URLs, and <li>Change how you form the request and parse the response. <p><strong>Example code</strong><br /></p><em>Before<br /></em><pre class=\"prettyprint\">// Request URL (JSON-RPC)<br />POST https://content.googleapis.com/rpc?alt=json&amp;key=xxx<br />// Request Body (JSON-RPC)<br />[{<br />  \"jsonrpc\":\"2.0\",<br />  \"id\":\"gapiRpc\",<br />  \"method\":\"zoo.animals.list\",<br />  \"apiVersion\":\"v2\",<br />  \"params\":{\"name\":\"giraffe\"}<br />}]<br /></pre><em>After</em><pre class=\"prettyprint\">// Request URL (JSON-REST)<br />GET <br />https://content.googleapis.com/zoo/v2/animals?name=giraffe&amp;key=xxx </pre> </li></li>\n   </ol><h2><strong><span style=\"text-decoration:underline;\">HTTP batch</span></strong></h2> <h2><strong>Endpoints</strong></h2> <p>The following Global HTTP Batch endpoints will no longer be supported. </p>\n   <ul> \n    <li>https://www.googleapis.com<strong>/batch</strong> <li>https://content.googleapis.com<strong>/batch</strong> <li>https://clients6.google.com<strong>/batch</strong></li></li></li>\n   </ul><p>Non-Global HTTP Batch endpoints that include the API name in the URI will continue to be supported. Examples includes: </p>\n   <ul> \n    <li>https://www.googleapis.com/batch/<strong><em>compute</em></strong>/v1 <li>https://content.googleapis.com/batch/<strong><em>compute</em></strong>/v1 <li>https://clients6.google.com/batch/<strong><em>compute</em></strong>/v1 <li>https://<strong>compute</strong>.googleapis.com/batch <li>https://content-<strong>compute</strong>.googleapis.com/batch <li>https://<strong><em>compute</em></strong>.clients6.google.com/batch</li></li></li></li></li></li>\n   </ul><h2> <strong>Heterogeneous batch requests</strong></h2> <p> If you are currently forming heterogeneous batch requests, change your client code to send only homogenous batch requests. </p><p> <strong>Example code<br /></strong>The example demonstrates how we can split a heterogeneous batch request for 2 apis (urlshortener and zoo) into 2 homogeneous batch requests. </p> <br><em>Before</em><br> <pre class=\"prettyprint\">// heterogeneous batch request example.<br /><br />// Notice that the outer batch request contains inner API requests<br />// for two different APIs.<br /><br />// Request to urlshortener API<br />request1 = gapi.client.urlshortener.url.get({\"shortUrl\": <br />\"http://goo.gl/fbsS\"});<br /><br />// Request to zoo API<br />request2 = gapi.client.zoo.animals.list();<br /><br />// Request to urlshortener API<br />request3 = gapi.client.urlshortener.url.get({\"shortUrl\":<br />\"https://goo.gl/XYFuPH\"});<br /><br />// Request to zoo API<br />request4 = gapi.client.zoo.animal().get({\"name\": \"giraffe\"});<br /><br />// Creating single heterogeneous batch request object<br />heterogeneousBatchRequest = gapi.client.newBatch();<br />// adding the 4 batch requests<br />heterogeneousBatchRequest.add(request1);<br />heterogeneousBatchRequest.add(request2);  <br />heterogeneousBatchRequest.add(request3);<br />heterogeneousBatchRequest.add(request4);<br />// print the heterogeneous batch request<br />heterogeneousBatchRequest.then(x=&gt;console.log(x));<br /><br /></pre> <br> <em>After</em><br> <pre class=\"prettyprint\">// Split heterogeneous batch request into two homogenous batch requests<br /><br />// Request to urlshortener API<br />request1 = gapi.client.urlshortener.url.get({\"shortUrl\": \"http://goo.gl/fbsS\"});<br /><br />// Request to zoo API<br />request2 = gapi.client.zoo.animals.list();<br /><br />// Request to urlshortener API<br />request3 = gapi.client.urlshortener.url.get({\"shortUrl\": \"http://goo.gl/fbsS\"})<br /><br />// Request to zoo API<br />request4 = gapi.client.zoo.animals.list();<br /><br />// Creating homogenous batch request object for urlshorterner<br />homogenousBatchUrlshortener = gapi.client.newBatch();<br />// adding the 2 batch requests for urlshorterner<br />homogenousBatchUrlshortener.add(request1); <br />homogenousBatchUrlshortener.add(request3); <br /><br />// Creating homogenous batch request object for zoo<br />homogenousBatchZoo = gapi.client.newBatch();<br /><br />// adding the 2 batch requests for zoo<br />homogenousBatchZoo.add(request2); <br />homogenousBatchZoo.add(request4);<br />// print the 2 homogenous batch request<br />Promise.all([homogenousBatchUrlshortener,homogenousBatchZoo])<br />    .then(x=&gt;console.log(x));<br /></pre> <h2> <strong>Homogeneous batch requests </strong></h2> <h2> <strong>Google API client libraries</strong></h2> <p> If you are using <a href=\"https://developers.google.com/api-client-library/\">Google API Client Libraries</a>, these libraries have been regenerated to no longer make requests to the global HTTP batch endpoint. Recommendation for clients using these libraries is to upgrade to the latest version if possible. Please see the language specific guidance below for minimum Google API Client Library to upgrade to. </p><strong>1. Java</strong>\n       <ol>\n        <ul> \n         <li>Minimum Google Client Library Version supported is 1.23.1. <li>Consumer Steps \n           <ol>\n            <li><p>Update all Google API Service packages (`com.google.apis`) to a version where the supporting library version is 1.23.1 or higher. For example, upgrade `com.google.apis:google-api-services-drive` from version `v3-rev159-1.22.0` to `v3-rev20190620-1.30.1`.</p></li> \n            <ol>\n             <li>If you explicitly import `com.google.api-client:google-api-client`, upgrade `com.google.api-client:google-api-client` to version 1.23.1 or higher.</li>\n            </ol> \n            <li> Please ensure you are creating your BatchRequest (i.e) <code>com.google.api.client.googleapis.batch.BatchRequest</code> instance via your service client. The BatchRequest constructor is now deprecated and will not work in the future. Instead, use your service client’s batch() method to create a new BatchRequest using below example </li>\n           </ol></li><p> <strong>Example code</strong></p> <pre class=\"prettyprint\">Drive client = Drive.builder(transport, jsonFactory, <br />credential).setApplicationName(\"BatchExample/1.0\").build<br />();<br /><p>BatchRequest batch = client.batch();<br /></p></pre> <li>For global batch, confirm that your code does not explicitly specify the Global Batch endpoint. <li><p> Rebuild</p></li> </li></li>\n        </ul>\n       </ol> <strong> 2. Python </strong> \n       <ul> \n        <li>Minimum Google Client Library Version supported is 1.6.6. <li>Consumer Steps \n          <ul> \n           <li>Update to version 1.6.6 or higher <li>Confirm that your code does not explicitly make a call to a Global HTTP Batch endpoint (e.g. www.googleapis.com/batch). These should be made to Non-Global HTTP Batch endpoints (e.g. www.googleapis.com/batch/compute/v1). <li>Rebuild </li> </li></li>\n          </ul> <li>Please note, a warning is included if users try to construct a request with the legacy batch endpoint. See <a href=\"https://github.com/googleapis/google-api-python-client/releases/tag/v1.6.6\">Release</a> notes for reference. </li> </li></li>\n       </ul> <strong>3. PHP</strong> \n       <ul> \n        <li>Minimum Google Client Library Version supported is 0.86. <li>Consumer Steps \n          <ul> \n           <li>Update to version 0.86 or higher <li>Confirm that your code does not explicitly make a call to a Global HTTP Batch endpoint (e.g. www.googleapis.com/batch). These should be made to Non-Global HTTP Batch endpoints (e.g. www.googleapis.com/batch/compute/v1). <li>Rebuild </li> </li></li>\n          </ul></li> </li>\n       </ul> <strong>4. .NET</strong> \n       <ul> \n        <li>Minimum Google Client Library Version supported is 1.32.2. <li>Consumer Steps \n          <ul> \n           <li>Update to version 1.32.2 or higher <li>Confirm that your code does not explicitly make a call to a Global HTTP Batch endpoint (e.g. www.googleapis.com/batch). These should be made to Non-Global HTTP Batch endpoints (e.g. www.googleapis.com/batch/compute/v1). <li>Rebuild </li> </li></li>\n          </ul></li> </li>\n       </ul> <strong>5. Javascript</strong> \n       <ul> \n        <li>If you are using Javascript client lib, please reach out to us with your questions and we will do our best to support </li> \n       </ul> <strong>6. Objective-C</strong> \n       <ul> \n        <li>Minimum Google Client Library Version supported is 1.3.0. <li>Consumer Steps \n          <ul> \n           <li>Update to version 1.3.0 or higher <li>Confirm that your code does not explicitly make a call to a Global HTTP Batch endpoint (e.g. www.googleapis.com/batch). These should be made to Non-Global HTTP Batch endpoints (e.g. www.googleapis.com/batch/compute/v1). <li>Rebuild </li> </li></li>\n          </ul></li> </li>\n       </ul> <strong>7. Dart</strong> \n       <ul> \n        <li>The Google API Dart Client Library does not support these features. </li>\n       </ul> <strong>8. Ruby</strong> \n       <ul> \n        <li>Minimum Google Client Library Version supported is 0.11.0. <li>Consumer Steps \n          <ul> \n           <li>Update to version 0.11.0 or higher <li>Confirm that your code does not explicitly make a call to a Global HTTP Batch endpoint (e.g. www.googleapis.com/batch). These should be made to Non-Global HTTP Batch endpoints (e.g. www.googleapis.com/batch/compute/v1). <li>Rebuild </li> </li></li>\n          </ul></li> </li>\n       </ul> <strong>9. Node.js</strong> \n       <ul> \n        <li>Minimum Google Client Library Version supported is 1.0. <li>Consumer Steps \n          <ul> \n           <li>Update to version 1.0 or higher <li>Confirm that your code does not explicitly make a call to a Global HTTP Batch endpoint (e.g. www.googleapis.com/batch). These should be made to Non-Global HTTP Batch endpoints (e.g. www.googleapis.com/batch/compute/v1). <li>Rebuild </li> </li></li>\n          </ul></li> </li>\n       </ul> <strong>10. Go</strong> \n       <ul> \n        <li>The Google API Go Client Library does not support these features. </li> \n       </ul> <strong>11. C++</strong> \n       <ul> \n        <li>The <a href=\"https://github.com/google/google-api-cpp-client\">Google C++ API Client Library</a> has been deprecated due to unrelated reasons. However, should you need to use the C++ client with batching in the short term, see consumer steps below. <li>Consumer Steps \n          <ul> \n           <li>Change app code to explicitly pass the non-global batch URL to the C++ client library i.e pass the API-version specific endpoint (e.g. \"<code>www.googleapis.com/batch/compute/v1</code>\") to the overload method that takes the batch endpoint as an explicit parameter; merely updating the C++ client library to the latest version will not help. <p> <strong>Example code</strong><br><em>Before</em><pre class=\"prettyprint\"><em>HttpRequestBatch batch(service-&gt;transport());</em></pre> <br><em>After</em> <pre class=\"prettyprint\">HttpRequestBatch batch(service-&gt;transport(), <br />service-&gt;batch_url());<br /></pre> <li>Link, rebuild and redeploy</li></br></br></p></li>\n          </ul></li></li>\n       </ul> <h2> <strong>Google Cloud Client Libraries</strong></h2> \n       <ol> \n        <li><strong>Java</strong><p> Upgrade to <a href=\"https://github.com/googleapis/google-cloud-java/tree/v0.57.0/google-cloud-clients/google-cloud-storage\">v1.39.0 or later of the Google Cloud Java Client for Storage</a> (released in <a href=\"https://github.com/googleapis/google-cloud-java/releases/tag/v0.57.0\">v0.57.0 of the Google Cloud Client Library</a>). </p> <li><strong>Python</strong><p> <a href=\"https://github.com/googleapis/python-storage/blob/master/CHANGELOG.md#190\">Upgrade to v1.9.0 or later of the GCS client</a>. </p></li></li>\n       </ol><h2>GCloud</h2><p>Older versions of gcloud used global batch calls in some cases. You should update your version of gcloudl. GCloud from v148.0.0 onwards is compatible with this deprecation.</p> <p>In general this can be done by running \"<a href=\"https://cloud.google.com/sdk/gcloud/reference/components/update\">gcloud components update</a>\".</p><h2>Apache Beam/ Cloud Dataflow</h2> <p>Users with Dataflow pipelines written using the <a href=\"https://cloud.google.com/dataflow/docs/support/sdk-version-support-status\">Beam (or Dataflow)</a> Python or Java SDKs 2.4 and below should update their pipelines to a later SDK (than 2.4), ideally to the latest one available here.</p> <h2> Dataproc hadoop connector </h2> <p>Users who run Apache Hadoop or Apache Spark jobs directly on data in Cloud Storage using gcs-connector should <a href=\"https://github.com/GoogleCloudDataproc/hadoop-connectors/releases/tag/v1.6.3\">update their connector to 1.6.3 or later</a>. </p> <h2><strong>Non-Google API client libraries or no client library</strong></h2> If you are currently forming homogeneous batch requests and using non-Google API client libraries or no client library (i.e making raw HTTP requests), then: </br></br></br></br></br></p>\n <ul> \n  <li>Change the endpoint from www.googleapis.com/batch to www.googleapis.com/batch/&lt;api&gt;/&lt;version&gt;. <li>Or, simply read the value of 'batchPath' from the API's discovery doc and use that value. </li></li>\n </ul>\n <h2><strong>We’re here to help</strong></h2> \n <p>For help on migration, consult the <a href=\"https://developers.google.com/products/\">API documentation</a> or tag Stack Overflow questions with the <a href=\"https://stackoverflow.com/tags/google-api/\">'google-api'</a> tag. </p>\n <img ","link":"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/GDBcode/~3/Eif6D40Ua6g/announcing-oauth-based-app-flip-for-actions.html","description":"<meta name=\"twitter:image\" src=\"https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-atnh_wEX2qI/XwNq9C6_ZjI/AAAAAAAAJFQ/ATFbkVMXU3Ad7Uy0ewYyGlSoMzCcOqBvACLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/OAuthAccountLinkingFlows.png\"> <p><em>Posted by Toni Klopfenstein, Developer Advocate</em><p> <p>Easy account linking helps create more helpful user experiences with Google Assistant and your products and services. Today, we are launching OAuth-based App Flip, a new feature to help you build a better mobile account linking experience. App Flip allows your users to seamlessly link their accounts to Google without having to re-enter their credentials if they have already signed in to your app on their device. This streamlined authorization flow helps minimize users dropping out of the account linking process, and makes it easier for users to integrate your smart devices into their smart homes. This feature is now available for all Smart Home Actions and is available in <a href=\"https://docs.google.com/forms/d/e/1FAIpQLSdZSd7lh675uFZ-Xb49xYx-HBv0jDoN0gsrjj3GBBGgyT5ELg/viewform\">beta</a> for other Conversational Actions.   </p><p>When App Flip is implemented within your application, the Google Assistant or Google Home app automatically flips to your app when users initiate the account linking process. Once users consent to link their accounts, your app then requests an authorization code from your server, and Google handles the remainder of the account linking flow.  </p> <center><a href=\"https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-atnh_wEX2qI/XwNq9C6_ZjI/AAAAAAAAJFQ/ATFbkVMXU3Ad7Uy0ewYyGlSoMzCcOqBvACLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/OAuthAccountLinkingFlows.png\" imageanchor=\"1\" ><img border=\"0\" src=\"https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-atnh_wEX2qI/XwNq9C6_ZjI/AAAAAAAAJFQ/ATFbkVMXU3Ad7Uy0ewYyGlSoMzCcOqBvACLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/OAuthAccountLinkingFlows.png\" data-original-width=\"583\" data-original-height=\"627\" /></a></center><p id=\"imgCaption\">Account Linking Flows</p><p>By flipping directly to your local app, users can skip logging in again and can simply choose to link their accounts.   </p><p>You can implement App Flip by enabling your app to accept a deep link that allows Google to connect. We also have test tools available for both <a href=\"https://github.com/googlesamples/identity-appflip-tester-android\">Android</a> and <a href=\"https://github.com/googlesamples/identity-appflip-tester-ios\">iOS</a> to help you verify your app integration with App Flip.  </p><p>For more details on how to use App Flip with your integration, check out the <a href=\"https://developers.google.com/assistant/smarthome/concepts/account-linking\">docs</a>, or the sample <a href=\"https://github.com/googlesamples/identity-appflip-android\">Android</a> and <a href=\"https://github.com/googlesamples/identity-appflip-ios\">iOS</a> apps.  For Conversational Actions, please <a href=\"https://docs.google.com/forms/d/e/1FAIpQLSdZSd7lh675uFZ-Xb49xYx-HBv0jDoN0gsrjj3GBBGgyT5ELg/viewform\">sign up for the Beta program</a>.  </p><p>We want to hear from you, so continue sharing your feedback with us, and engage with other Action developers in the <a href=\"https://www.reddit.com/r/GoogleAssistantDev\">/r/GoogleAssistantDev</a> community. Follow <a href=\"https://twitter.com/ActionsOnGoogle\">@ActionsOnGoogle</a> on Twitter for more of our team's updates, and tweet using #AoGDevs to share what you’re working on. We can’t wait to see what you build! </p><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/GDBcode/~4/Eif6D40Ua6g\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\"/>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Wed, 08 Jul Run","link":"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/GDBcode/~3/IYUfvbF-U_I/automatic-deployment-of-hugo-sites-on-firebase-hosting.html","description":"<meta name=\"twitter:image\" content=\"https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-dTUssho8JBU/XyikkAQSJhI/AAAAAAAAJL8/3nwp99zcL9ITwxkhOLtOuSwJ4rRY5fR_QCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/hugostarterrepo.png\"><img style=\"display:none\" src=\"https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-dTUssho8JBU/XyikkAQSJhI/AAAAAAAAJL8/3nwp99zcL9ITwxkhOLtOuSwJ4rRY5fR_QCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/hugostarterrepo.png\"> <p><em>Posted by <a href=\"https://twitter.com/_jamesward?lang=en\">James Ward</a>, Developer Advocate</em><p> <p>Recently I completed the migration of <a href=\"http://jamesward.com\">my blog</a> from Wordpress to Hugo and I wanted to take advantage of it now being a static site by hosting it on a Content Delivery Network (CDN).  With Hugo the source content is plain files instead of rows in a database.  In the case of my blog those files are in git on GitHub.  But when the source files change, the site needs to be regenerated and redeployed to the CDN.  Also, sometimes it is nice to have drafts available for review.  I setup a continuous delivery pipeline which deploys changes to my prod site on Firebase Hosting and drafts on Cloud Run, using Cloud Build.  Read on for instructions for how to set all this up. </p><h2>Step 1a) Setup A New Hugo Project</h2>If you do not have an existing Hugo project you can create a <a href=\"https://github.com/jamesward/hello-hugo/fork\">GitHub copy</a> (i.e. fork) of my Hugo starter repo: <a href=\"https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-dTUssho8JBU/XyikkAQSJhI/AAAAAAAAJL8/3nwp99zcL9ITwxkhOLtOuSwJ4rRY5fR_QCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/hugostarterrepo.png\" imageanchor=\"1\" ><img border=\"0\" src=\"https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-dTUssho8JBU/XyikkAQSJhI/AAAAAAAAJL8/3nwp99zcL9ITwxkhOLtOuSwJ4rRY5fR_QCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/hugostarterrepo.png\" data-original-width=\"1040\" data-original-height=\"806\" /></a><h2>Step 1b) Setup Existing Hugo Project</h2><p>If you have an existing Hugo project you'll need to add some files to it: </p><p><code>.firebaserc</code></p>   <pre class=\"prettyprint\">{<br />  \"projects\": {<br />    \"production\": \"hello-hugo\"<br />  }<br />}</pre>  <p><code>cloudbuild-draft.yaml</code></p>   <pre class=\"prettyprint\">steps:<br />- name: 'gcr.io/cloud-builders/git'<br />  entrypoint: '/bin/sh'<br />  args:<br />  - '-c'<br />  - |<br />    # Get the theme git submodule<br />    THEME_URL=$(git config -f .gitmodules --get-regexp '^submodule\\..*\\.url$' | awk '{ print $2 }')<br />    THEME_DIR=$(git config -f .gitmodules --get-regexp '^submodule\\..*\\.path$' | awk '{ print $2 }')<br />    rm -rf themes<br />    git clone $$THEME_URL $$THEME_DIR<br /><br />- name: 'gcr.io/cloud-builders/docker'<br />  entrypoint: '/bin/sh'<br />  args:<br />  - '-c'<br />  - |<br />    docker build -t gcr.io/$PROJECT_ID/$REPO_NAME-$BRANCH_NAME:$COMMIT_SHA -f - . &lt;&lt; EOF<br />    FROM klakegg/hugo:latest<br />    WORKDIR /workspace<br />    COPY . /workspace<br />    ENTRYPOINT hugo -D -p \\$$PORT --bind \\$$HUGO_BIND --renderToDisk --disableLiveReload --watch=false serve<br />    EOF<br />    docker push gcr.io/$PROJECT_ID/$REPO_NAME-$BRANCH_NAME:$COMMIT_SHA<br /><br />- name: 'gcr.io/cloud-builders/gcloud'<br />  args:<br />  - run<br />  - deploy<br />  - --image=gcr.io/$PROJECT_ID/$REPO_NAME-$BRANCH_NAME:$COMMIT_SHA<br />  - --platform=managed<br />  - --project=$PROJECT_ID<br />  - --region=us-central1<br />  - --memory=512Mi<br />  - --allow-unauthenticated<br />  - $REPO_NAME-$BRANCH_NAME</pre>  <p><code>cloudbuild.yaml</code></p>   <pre class=\"prettyprint\">steps:<br />- name: 'gcr.io/cloud-builders/git'<br />  entrypoint: '/bin/sh'<br />  args:<br />  - '-c'<br />  - |<br />    # Get the theme git submodule<br />    THEME_URL=$(git config -f .gitmodules --get-regexp '^submodule\\..*\\.url$' | awk '{ print $2 }')<br />    THEME_DIR=$(git config -f .gitmodules --get-regexp '^submodule\\..*\\.path$' | awk '{ print $2 }')<br />    rm -rf themes<br />    git clone $$THEME_URL $$THEME_DIR<br /><br />- name: 'gcr.io/cloud-builders/curl'<br />  entrypoint: '/bin/sh'<br />  args:<br />  - '-c'<br />  - |<br />    curl -sL https://github.com/gohugoio/hugo/releases/download/v0.69.2/hugo_0.69.2_Linux-64bit.tar.gz | tar -zxv<br />    ./hugo<br /><br />- name: 'gcr.io/cloud-builders/wget'<br />  entrypoint: '/bin/sh'<br />  args:<br />  - '-c'<br />  - |<br />    # Get firebase CLI<br />    wget -O firebase https://firebase.tools/bin/linux/latest<br />    chmod +x firebase<br />    # Deploy site<br />    ./firebase deploy --project=$PROJECT_ID --only=hosting</pre>  <p><code>firebase.json</code></p>   <pre class=\"prettyprint\">{<br />  \"hosting\": {<br />    \"public\": \"public\"<br />  }<br />}</pre><br></br><h2>Step 2) Setup Cloud Build Triggers</h2>In the Google Cloud Build console, <a href=\"https://console.cloud.google.com/cloud-build/triggers/connect\">connect to your newly forked repo</a>:  <a href=\"https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-WsgNBXJGTrU/XyimivpxIpI/AAAAAAAAJMI/h0vFwC4Pd844vgVoAU24M8bimyUER_17gCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/newlyforkedrepo.png\" imageanchor=\"1\" ><img border=\"0\" src=\"https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-WsgNBXJGTrU/XyimivpxIpI/AAAAAAAAJMI/h0vFwC4Pd844vgVoAU24M8bimyUER_17gCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/newlyforkedrepo.png\" data-original-width=\"1040\" data-original-height=\"806\" /></a> Select the newly forked repo:  <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-UfsIwy8ecno/XyimqWZJHWI/AAAAAAAAJMM/t7PXafKqElghnHo6N3Autz9rx7AIzORCACLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/selectthenewlyforkedrepo.png\" imageanchor=\"1\" ><img border=\"0\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-UfsIwy8ecno/XyimqWZJHWI/AAAAAAAAJMM/t7PXafKqElghnHo6N3Autz9rx7AIzORCACLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/selectthenewlyforkedrepo.png\" data-original-width=\"1040\" data-original-height=\"806\" /></a> Create the default push trigger:  <a href=\"https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-HTx8QE6X2Dc/XyisiDlJpuI/AAAAAAAAJNo/v3XruX4tDQwd5AumtVHSag85wYylE-lNACLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/pasted%2Bimage%2B0.png\" imageanchor=\"1\" ><img border=\"0\" src=\"https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-HTx8QE6X2Dc/XyisiDlJpuI/AAAAAAAAJNo/v3XruX4tDQwd5AumtVHSag85wYylE-lNACLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/pasted%2Bimage%2B0.png\" data-original-width=\"1040\" data-original-height=\"806\" /></a>Edit the new trigger: <a href=\"https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-xZx_vjXKxoY/Xyim7fV0SBI/AAAAAAAAJMc/Lx19fESrcxY9kaJFgmYGKRLGDvwysF4AACLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/editnewtrigger.png\" imageanchor=\"1\" ><img border=\"0\" src=\"https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-xZx_vjXKxoY/Xyim7fV0SBI/AAAAAAAAJMc/Lx19fESrcxY9kaJFgmYGKRLGDvwysF4AACLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/editnewtrigger.png\" data-original-width=\"1040\" data-original-height=\"806\" /></a> Set the trigger to only fire on changes to the <code>^master$</code> branch:  <a href=\"https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-ZJTCaEHfVhA/XyinAef77CI/AAAAAAAAJMg/CFRr6-plhhwsbi3QXsmBg9tlE1e3ivRpACLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/triggerbranch.png\" imageanchor=\"1\" ><img border=\"0\" src=\"https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-ZJTCaEHfVhA/XyinAef77CI/AAAAAAAAJMg/CFRr6-plhhwsbi3QXsmBg9tlE1e3ivRpACLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/triggerbranch.png\" data-original-width=\"1040\" data-original-height=\"806\" /></a> Create a new trigger:  <a href=\"https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-MjewTREGSpU/XyinEx05eoI/AAAAAAAAJMk/g-KWZJNLq4s115uUllqmit_Ei55Ox0nlwCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/createnewtrigger.png\" imageanchor=\"1\" ><img border=\"0\" src=\"https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-MjewTREGSpU/XyinEx05eoI/AAAAAAAAJMk/g-KWZJNLq4s115uUllqmit_Ei55Ox0nlwCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/createnewtrigger.png\" data-original-width=\"1040\" data-original-height=\"806\" /></a> Give it a name like <code>drafts-trigger</code>, specify the branch selector as <code>.*</code> (i.e. any branch), and the build configuration file type to \"Cloud Build configuration file\" with a value of <code>cloudbuild-draft.yaml</code> <a href=\"https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-0q0lbra3mlo/XyindT2AwkI/AAAAAAAAJM4/46Vq0eRSr-MO7MtwlgEComgxYUEF0oXFwCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/giveitaname.png\" imageanchor=\"1\" ><img border=\"0\" src=\"https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-0q0lbra3mlo/XyindT2AwkI/AAAAAAAAJM4/46Vq0eRSr-MO7MtwlgEComgxYUEF0oXFwCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/giveitaname.png\" data-original-width=\"1040\" data-original-height=\"806\" /></a> Setup permissions for the Cloud Build process to manage Cloud Run and Firebase Hosting by visiting the IAM management page, locate the member with the name ending with <code>@cloudbuild.gserviceaccount.com</code>, and select the \"pencil\" / edit button:  <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-TNxjJQy_zoM/XyinnEdk8MI/AAAAAAAAJM8/g3azkrzM9hkKJdcFtVs6yQzQsvlmRwRYwCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/setuppermissions.png\" imageanchor=\"1\" ><img border=\"0\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-TNxjJQy_zoM/XyinnEdk8MI/AAAAAAAAJM8/g3azkrzM9hkKJdcFtVs6yQzQsvlmRwRYwCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/setuppermissions.png\" data-original-width=\"1040\" data-original-height=\"804\" /></a> Add a role for \"Cloud Run Admin\" and another for \"Firebase Hosting Admin\":  <a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-Ees8pQRhljI/XyinrJJFlGI/AAAAAAAAJNA/GYs2QjgGK54cWOrHtODIyrRRLdIoFU1QgCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/addrole.png\" imageanchor=\"1\" ><img border=\"0\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-Ees8pQRhljI/XyinrJJFlGI/AAAAAAAAJNA/GYs2QjgGK54cWOrHtODIyrRRLdIoFU1QgCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/addrole.png\" data-original-width=\"1040\" data-original-height=\"804\" /></a> Your default \"prod\" trigger isn't read to test yet, but you can test the drafts on Cloud Run by going back to <a href=\"https://console.cloud.google.com/cloud-build/triggers\">the Cloud Build Triggers page</a>, and clicking the \"Run Trigger\" button on the \"drafts-trigger\" line.  Check the build logs by finding the build in the <a href=\"https://console.cloud.google.com/cloud-build/builds\">Cloud Build History</a>.  Once the build completes <a href=\"https://console.cloud.google.com/run\">visit the Cloud Run console</a> to find your newly created service which hosts the drafts version of your new blog.  Note that the service name includes the branch so that you can see drafts from different branches. <br></br><h2>Step 3) Setup Firebase Hosting</h2>To setup your production / CDN'd site, <a href=\"https://console.firebase.google.com\">login to the firebase console</a> and select your project: <a href=\"https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-Ar6RW2zlR1w/XyipsG-5QwI/AAAAAAAAJNU/NGeQ4ved7SsW6mcjwWxDVhYs54l49ka6wCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/firebasehosting.png\" imageanchor=\"1\" ><img border=\"0\" src=\"https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-Ar6RW2zlR1w/XyipsG-5QwI/AAAAAAAAJNU/NGeQ4ved7SsW6mcjwWxDVhYs54l49ka6wCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/firebasehosting.png\" data-original-width=\"1040\" data-original-height=\"804\" /></a><p>Now you'll need your project id, which can be found in the URL on the Firebase Project Overview page.  The URL for my project is: </p><p><a href=\"https://console.firebase.google.com/project/jw-demo/overview\">console.firebase.google.com/project/jw-demo/overview</a></p><p>Which means my project id is: jw-demo </p><p>Now copy your project id go into your GitHub fork, select the <code>.firebaserc</code> file and click the \"pencil\" / edit button: </p><a href=\"https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-9PNXSkk0vYQ/XyiqtWp7AvI/AAAAAAAAJNc/GhBuKHyQEa0nvwtXAweoKg0O-GSy70G1QCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/hellohugo.png\" imageanchor=\"1\" ><img border=\"0\" src=\"https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-9PNXSkk0vYQ/XyiqtWp7AvI/AAAAAAAAJNc/GhBuKHyQEa0nvwtXAweoKg0O-GSy70G1QCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/hellohugo.png\" data-original-width=\"1040\" data-original-height=\"804\" /></a><p>Replace the <code>hello-hugo</code> string with your project id and commit the changes.  This commit will trigger two new builds, one for the production site and one for the drafts site on Cloud Run.  You can check the status of those builds on the <a href=\"https://console.cloud.google.com/cloud-build/builds\">Cloud Build History page</a>.  Once the default trigger (the one for Firebase hosting) finishes, check out your Hugo site running on Firebase Hosting by navigating to (replacing YOUR_PROJECT_ID with the project id you used above): https://YOUR_PROJECT_ID.web.app/ </p><p>Your prod and drafts sites are now automatically deploying on new commits! </p><h2>Step 4) (Optional) Change Hugo Theme</h2><p>There are <a href=\"https://themes.gohugo.io/\">many themes for Hugo</a> and they are easy to change.  Typically themes are pulled into Hugo sites using git submodules.  To change the theme, edit your <code>.gitmodules</code> file and set the subdirectories and url.  As an example, here is the content when using the mainroad theme: </p>   <pre class=\"prettyprint\">[submodule \"themes/mainroad\"]<br /> path = themes/mainroad<br /> url = https://github.com/vimux/mainroad.git<br /></pre>  <p>You will also need to change the <code>theme</code> value in your <code>config.toml</code> file to match the directory name in the <code>themes</code> directory.  For example: </p>   <pre class=\"prettyprint\">theme = \"mainroad\"<br /></pre>  <p>Note: At the time of writing this, Cloud Build does not clone git submodules so the <code>cloudbuild.yaml</code> <a href=\"https://github.com/jamesward/hello-hugo/blob/master/cloudbuild.yaml#L2-L11\">does the cloning</a> instead. </p> <h2>Step 5) (Optional) Setup Local Editing</h2><p>To setup local editing you will first need to clone your fork.  You can do this with the <a href=\"https://desktop.github.com/\">GitHub desktop app</a>.  Or from the command line: </p>  <pre class=\"prettyprint\">git clone --recurse-submodules https://github.com/USER/REPO.git<br /></pre>  <p>Once you have the files locally, <a href=\"https://gohugo.io/getting-started/installing/\">install Hugo</a>, and from inside the repo's directory, run: </p>   <pre class=\"prettyprint\">hugo -D serve<br /></pre>  <p>This will serve the drafts in the site.  You can check out the site at: localhost:1313 </p><p>Committing non-draft changes to master and pushing those changes to GitHub will kick off the build which will deploy them on your prod site.  Committing draft to any branch will kick off the build which will deploy them on a Cloud Run site. </p><p>Hopefully that all helps you with hosting your Hugo sites!  <a href=\"https://github.com/jamesward/hello-hugo/issues\">Let me know if you run into any problems</a>. </p><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/GDBcode/~4/IYUfvbF-U_I\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" 08:46:09","updatedTime":"2020-08-25 08:46:09","title":"Simpler Google Pay integration for React and web developers","link":"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/GDBcode/~3/3Y6s4CmPfQY/simpler-google-pay-integration-for-react-web-developers.html","description":"<meta name=\"twitter:image\" content=\"https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-yTY5ffcuNk4/XvDXkgBjHhI/AAAAAAAAI7M/6qJYLQtRhAgRLNePVHKpaFI1KQI6FK0fQCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/googlepaybanner.png\"><img style=\"display:none\" src=\"https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-yTY5ffcuNk4/XvDXkgBjHhI/AAAAAAAAI7M/6qJYLQtRhAgRLNePVHKpaFI1KQI6FK0fQCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/googlepaybanner.png\"> <p><em>Posted by Soc Sieng, Developer Advocate</em><p><a href=\"https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-yTY5ffcuNk4/XvDXkgBjHhI/AAAAAAAAI7M/6qJYLQtRhAgRLNePVHKpaFI1KQI6FK0fQCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/googlepaybanner.png\" imageanchor=\"1\" ><img border=\"0\" src=\"https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-yTY5ffcuNk4/XvDXkgBjHhI/AAAAAAAAI7M/6qJYLQtRhAgRLNePVHKpaFI1KQI6FK0fQCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/googlepaybanner.png\" data-original-width=\"1600\" data-original-height=\"604\" /></a>The Google Pay API enables fast, simple checkout for your website.  <p>The Google Pay JavaScript library does not depend on external libraries or frameworks and will work regardless of which framework your website uses (if it uses any at all). While this ensures wide compatibility, we know that it doesn’t necessarily make it easier to integrate when your website uses a framework. We’re doing something about it.</p><h2>Introducing the Google Pay button for React</h2><p>React is one of the most widely-used tools for building web UI's, so we are launching the <a href=\"https://github.com/google-pay/google-pay-button/tree/main/src/button-react\">Google Pay Button for React</a> to provide a streamlined integration experience. This component will make it easier to incorporate Google Pay into your React website whether you are new to React or a seasoned pro, and similarly, if this is your first Google Pay integration or if you’ve done this before. </p><p>We’re making this component available as an open source project on <a href=\"https://github.com/google-pay/google-pay-button/tree/main/src/button-react\">GitHub</a> and publishing it to <a href=\"https://www.npmjs.com/package/@google-pay/button-react\">npm</a>. We’ve authored the React component with TypeScript to bring code completion to supported editors, and if your website is built with TypeScript you can also take advantage of type validation to identify common issues as you type. </p><a href=\"https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-qLHOWEa8GH0/XvDXppDuSFI/AAAAAAAAI7Q/K-EqZBzdIR4ViGxM03gjHtTYK-frsoxJACLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/realtimecode.gif\" imageanchor=\"1\" ><img id=\"imgFull\" border=\"0\" src=\"https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-qLHOWEa8GH0/XvDXppDuSFI/AAAAAAAAI7Q/K-EqZBzdIR4ViGxM03gjHtTYK-frsoxJACLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/realtimecode.gif\" data-original-width=\"1095\" data-original-height=\"784\" /></a><p id=\"imgCaption\">Get real time code completion and validation as you integrate with supported editors.</p><h3>Getting started</h3><p>The first step is to install the Google Pay button module from npm:</p><pre class=\"prettyprint\">npm install @google-pay/button-react</pre><h3>Adding and configuring the button</h3><p>The Google Pay button can be added to your React component by first importing it:</p><pre class=\"prettyprint\">import GooglePayButton from '@google-pay/button-react';</pre><p>And then rendering it with the necessary configuration values:</p><pre class=\"prettyprint\">&lt;GooglePayButton<br />  environment=\"TEST\"<br />  paymentRequest={{ ... }}<br />  onLoadPaymentData={() => {}}<br />  /></pre><p>Try it out for yourself on <a href=\"https://jsfiddle.net/1Lwndx7b/\">JSFiddle</a>.</p><p>Refer to <a href=\"https://github.com/google-pay/google-pay-button/tree/main/src/button-react#documentation\">component documentation</a> for a full list of supported configuration properties. </p><p>Note that you will need to provide a Merchant ID in <code>paymentRequest.merchantInfo</code> to complete the integration. Your Merchant ID can be obtained from the <a href=\"https://pay.google.com/business/console?utm_source=google_dev_blog&utm_medium=article&utm_campaign=business_console_launch\">Google Pay Business Console</a>. </p><a href=\"https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-Xg40TDM3rh8/XvDYcX3QevI/AAAAAAAAI7Y/Hj8bTXoJgsEGfBc3xy7arTluNXXebm3lgCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/merchantID.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" ><img id=\"imgFull\" border=\"0\" src=\"https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-Xg40TDM3rh8/XvDYcX3QevI/AAAAAAAAI7Y/Hj8bTXoJgsEGfBc3xy7arTluNXXebm3lgCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/merchantID.jpg\" data-original-width=\"1440\" data-original-height=\"1024\" /></a><p id=\"imgCaption\">Your Merchant ID can be found in the Google Pay Business Console.</p><h2>Support for other frameworks</h2><p>We also want to provide an improved developer experience for our developers using other frameworks, or no framework at all. That’s why we are also releasing the <a href=\"https://github.com/google-pay/google-pay-button/tree/main/src/button-element\">Google Pay button Custom Element</a>. </p><p>Custom elements are great because: </p><ul> <li>They are part of the Web Component specification and are <a href=\"https://caniuse.com/#feat=custom-elementsv1\">supported by most modern browsers</a> <li>They work well with other frameworks (see <a href=\"https://custom-elements-everywhere.com/\">Custom Elements Everywhere</a> for more information)  <li>They work without a framework </li></ul><p>Like the React component, the Google Pay button custom element is hosted on <a href=\"https://github.com/google-pay/google-pay-button/tree/main/src/button-element\">GitHub</a> and published to <a href=\"https://www.npmjs.com/package/@google-pay/button-element\">npm</a>. In fact, the React component and the custom element share the same repository and large portion of code. This ensures that both versions maintain feature parity and receive the same level of care and attention. </p><p>Try it out on <a href=\"https://jsfiddle.net/f70e8nx4/\">JSFiddle.</a></p><h2>Google Pay JavaScript library</h2><p>There's no change to the existing Google Pay JavaScript library, and if you prefer, you can continue to use this directly instead of the React component or custom element. Both of these components provide a convenience layer over the Google Pay JavaScript library and make use of it internally.</p><h2>Your feedback</h2><p>This is the first time that we (the Google Pay team) have released a framework specific library. We would love to hear your feedback. </p><p>Aside from React, most frameworks can use the Web Component version of the Google Pay Button. We may consider adding support for other frameworks based on interest and demand. </p><p>If you encounter any problems with the React component or custom element, please raise a <a href=\"https://github.com/google-pay/google-pay-button/issues\">GitHub issue</a>. Alternatively, if you know what the problem is and have a solution in mind, feel free to raise a pull request. For other Google Pay related requests and questions, use the Contact Support option in the <a href=\"https://pay.google.com/business/console?utm_source=google_dev_blog&utm_medium=article&utm_campaign=business_console_launch\">Google Pay Business Console</a>. </p><h3>What do you think?</h3>Do you have any questions? data-original-width=\"1600\" data-original-height=\"481\" /></a><i>This article originally appeared on ChromeOS.dev.</i><p>While people are spending more time at home than on the go, they’re relying increasingly on personal desktops and laptops to make everyday life easier. Whether they’re video-chatting with friends and family, discovering entertaining apps and games, multitasking at work, or pursuing a passion project, bigger screens and better performance have made all the difference. </p><p>This trend was clear from March through June 2020: Chromebook unit sales grew 127% year over year (YOY) while the rest of the U.S. notebook category increased by 40% YOY.<sup>1</sup> Laptops have become crucial to people at home who want to use their favorite apps and games, like <a href=\"https://play.google.com/store/apps/details?id=com.scopely.startrek&hl=en_US\">Star Trek™ Fleet Command</a> and <a href=\"https://play.google.com/store/apps/details?id=com.devolver.reignsGot&hl=en_US\">Reigns: Game of Thrones</a> to enjoy action-packed adventure, <a href=\"https://play.google.com/store/apps/details?id=com.calm.android&hl=en_US\">Calm</a> to manage stress, or <a href=\"https://play.google.com/store/apps/details?id=com.disney.disneyplus&hl=en_US\">Disney+</a> to keep the whole family entertained. </p><a href=\"https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-aJlWUS7129s/XzMRz_6P4dI/AAAAAAAAJPs/M8UQnVDiA2klXBp3msHDpEk-6D-Rl350ACLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/deviceyoy.gif\" imageanchor=\"1\" ><img border=\"0\" src=\"https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-aJlWUS7129s/XzMRz_6P4dI/AAAAAAAAJPs/M8UQnVDiA2klXBp3msHDpEk-6D-Rl350ACLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/deviceyoy.gif\" data-original-width=\"1477\" data-original-height=\"744\" alt=\"Device Sales YOY\"/></a><p>To deliver app experiences that truly improve people’s lives, developers must be equipped with the right tools, resources, and best practices. That’s why we’re excited to introduce <strong><a href=\"https://chromeos.dev/en/\">ChromeOS.dev </a></strong>— a dedicated resource for technical developers, designers, product managers, and business leaders. </p><p>ChromeOS.dev, available in English and Spanish (with other languages coming soon), features the latest news, product announcements, technical documentation, and code samples from popular apps. Whether you’re a web, Android, or Linux developer who’s just getting started or a certified expert, you’ll find all the information you need on ChromeOS.dev. </p><p>Hear from our experts at Google and Chrome OS, as well as a variety of developers, as they share practical tips, benefits, and the challenges of creating app experiences for today’s users. Plus, you can review the updated <a href=\"https://chromeos.dev/en/android/design\">Chrome OS Layout and UX App Quality guidelines</a> with helpful information on UI components, navigation, fonts, layouts, and everything that goes into creating world-class apps and games for Chrome OS. </p><p>Even better, as a <a href=\"https://github.com/chromeos/chromeos.dev\">fully open-source</a> online destination, ChromeOS.dev is designed considering all the principles and methods for creating highly capable and reliable Progressive Web Apps (PWAs), ensuring developers always have quick, easy access to the information they need — even when they’re offline. </p><a href=\"https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-DPouUK8To1E/XzMSRcCAfGI/AAAAAAAAJP0/-qHt1nFvTGgj0J42-mu64rOA16COksY-gCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/chromeos.gif\" imageanchor=\"1\" ><img border=\"0\" src=\"https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-DPouUK8To1E/XzMSRcCAfGI/AAAAAAAAJP0/-qHt1nFvTGgj0J42-mu64rOA16COksY-gCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/chromeos.gif\" data-original-width=\"800\" data-original-height=\"419\" /></a><p>Check out a few of the newest updates and improvements below, and be sure to install the ChromeOS.dev PWA on your device to stay on top of the latest information.  </p><h2>New features for Chrome OS developers</h2><p>Whether it’s developing Android, Linux, or web apps, every update on ChromeOS.dev is about making sure all developers can build better app experiences in a streamlined, easy-to-navigate environment. </p><h3>Customizable Linux Terminal</h3><p>The Linux (Beta) on Chrome OS Terminal now comes equipped with personalized features right out of the box, including:</p><ul><li><b>Integrated tabs and shortcuts</b><br>Multitask with ease by using windows and tabs to manage different tasks and switch between multiple projects. You can also use familiar shortcuts such as Ctrl + T, Ctrl + W, and Ctrl + Tab to manage your tabs, or use the settings page to control if these keys should be used in your Terminal for apps like vim or emacs. <li><b>Themes</b><br>Customize your Terminal by selecting a theme to switch up the background, frame, font, and cursor color. <a href=\"https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-7b6WatO6EfA/XzM01pbtRwI/AAAAAAAAJQA/OcvDS48Iwc063kPy55FewRqpYHZ25RxEgCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/linuxtheme.gif\" imageanchor=\"1\" ><img style=\"width:100%\" border=\"0\" src=\"https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-7b6WatO6EfA/XzM01pbtRwI/AAAAAAAAJQA/OcvDS48Iwc063kPy55FewRqpYHZ25RxEgCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/linuxtheme.gif\" data-original-width=\"800\" data-original-height=\"450\" /></a><li><b>Redesigned Terminal settings</b><br>The settings tab has been reorganized to make it easier to customize all your Terminal options. </li></ul><p>Developers can now start using these and other customizable features in the Terminal app. </p><h3>Android Emulator support</h3><p><a href=\"https://chromeos.dev/en/android-environment\">Supported Chromebooks</a> can now run a full version of the Android Emulator, which allows developers to test apps on any Android version and device without needing the actual hardware. Android app developers can simulate <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/studio/run/emulator#extended\">map locations</a> and other sensor data to test how an app performs with various motions, orientations, and environmental conditions. With the Android Emulator support in Chrome OS, developers can optimize for different Android versions and devices — including tablets and<a href=\"https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/ui/foldables#emulators\"> foldable smartphones</a> — right from their Chromebook. </p><h3>Deploy apps directly to Chrome OS</h3><p>Building and testing Android apps on a single machine is simpler than ever. Now, developers who are running Chrome OS M81 and higher can<a href=\"https://chromeos.dev/en/android-environment/deploying-apps\"> deploy and test apps directly on their Chromebooks</a>  — no need to use developer mode or to connect different devices physically via USB. Combined with Android Emulator support, Chrome OS is equipped to support full Android development. </p><h3>Improved Project Wizard in Android Studio</h3><p>An updated <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/studio/projects/templates#PrimaryDetailFlow\">Primary/Detail Activity Template</a> in Android Studio offers complete support to build experiences for larger screens, including Chromebooks, tablets, and foldables. This updated option provides multiple layouts for both phones and larger-screen devices as well as better keyboard/mouse scaffolding. This feature will be available in Android Studio 4.2 Canary 8. </p><h3>Updated support from Android lint checks</h3><p>We’ve improved the default checks in <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/studio/write/lint\">Android’s lint tool</a> to help developers identify and correct common coding issues to improve their apps on larger screens, such as non-resizable and portrait-locked activities. This feature is currently available for testing in Canary channel. </p><h2>Unlock your app’s full potential with Chrome OS</h2><p>From day one, our goal has been to help developers at every skill level create simple, powerful, and secure app experiences for all platforms. As our new reality creates a greater need for helpful and engaging apps on large-screen devices, we’re working hard to streamline the process by making Chrome OS more versatile, customizable, and intuitive.  </p><p>Visit ChromeOS.dev and install it on your Chromebook to stay on top of the latest resources, product updates, thought-provoking insights, and inspiring success stories from Chrome OS developers worldwide. </p><br></br><br></br><hr></hr><small><p>Sources:<br><sup>1 </sup>The NPD Group, Inc., U.S. Retail Tracking Service, Notebook Computers, based on unit sales, April–June 2020 WiFi","link":"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/GDBcode/~3/2jMyrlXiS1Y/local-home-sdk-support-on-google-nest-wifi.html","description":"<meta name=\"twitter:image\" content=\"https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-VNmy5ycvBjA/Xuex_FZrrVI/AAAAAAAAI5k/Jcxx3ItolWYfgAtydRStO11Z0aDNdIgjQCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/MistralAoGH.jpeg\"><img style=\"display:none\" src=\"https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-VNmy5ycvBjA/Xuex_FZrrVI/AAAAAAAAI5k/Jcxx3ItolWYfgAtydRStO11Z0aDNdIgjQCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/MistralAoGH.jpeg\"> <p><em>Posted by Toni Klopfenstein, Developer Advocate</em></p> <p>Today, we're expanding the support of the Local Home SDK to the Google Nest Wifi routers with the <a href=\"https://support.google.com/googlenest/answer/9911425?hl=en\">latest firmware update to M81</a>. The Local Home SDK we <a href=\"https://developers.googleblog.com/2020/04/local-home-sdk-ready-for-actions.html\">recently launched</a> allows you  to create a local fulfilment path for your smart home Action. Local fulfillment provides lower latency and higher reliability for your smart home Action.  </p><p>By adding support for the Node.js runtime of the Nest WiFi routers, the Local Home platform is now compatible with the full Nest WiFi system. This update means your local execution application can run on a self-healing mesh wireless network, and your users gain the benefits of expanded reliable home automation coverage.  </p><a href=\"https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-VNmy5ycvBjA/Xuex_FZrrVI/AAAAAAAAI5k/Jcxx3ItolWYfgAtydRStO11Z0aDNdIgjQCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/MistralAoGH.jpeg\" imageanchor=\"1\" ><img border=\"0\" src=\"https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-VNmy5ycvBjA/Xuex_FZrrVI/AAAAAAAAI5k/Jcxx3ItolWYfgAtydRStO11Z0aDNdIgjQCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/MistralAoGH.jpeg\" data-original-width=\"962\" data-original-height=\"542\" /></a><p>To support this additional runtime, we've updated the <a href=\"http://console.actions.google.com\">Actions Console</a> to enable you to add the Node.js on-device testing URL. The Nest WiFi routers will receive the the node-targeted <code>bundle.js</code> files you've already uploaded during deployment of your Action automatically.  Since <a href=\"https://developers.google.com/assistant/smarthome/develop/local#debugging_from_chrome\">Chrome DevTools</a> have built-in Node.js support, your development flow doesn't require any additional tools for inspecting your Node.js app or debugging your smart home Action.  </p><p>We have updated the <a href=\"https://developers.google.com/assistant/smarthome/concepts/local\">developer guide</a> and tools to help guide you through the <a href=\"https://developers.google.com/assistant/smarthome/concepts/local#execution-environment\">various local fulfilment runtimes</a> and features of these toolings. For additional guidance on enabling local fulfilment for your smart home Action, check out the <a href=\"https://codelabs.developers.google.com/codelabs/smarthome-local/index.html?index=..%2F..index#0\">Enable local fulfillment for smart home Actions codelab</a>. The <a href=\"https://developers.google.com/assistant/smarthome/reference/local\">API reference</a> and <a href=\"https://github.com/actions-on-google/smart-home-local\">samples</a> can also help you build your first local fulfilment app.  </p><p>We want to hear from you! Continue sharing your feedback with us through the <a href=\"https://issuetracker.google.com/issues/new?component=655104&template=1284327\">issue tracker</a>, and engage with other smart home developers in the <a href=\"https://www.reddit.com/r/GoogleAssistantDev\">/r/GoogleAssistantDev</a> community. Follow <a href=\"https://twitter.com/ActionsOnGoogle\">@ActionsOnGoogle</a> on Twitter for more of our team's updates, and tweet using #AoGDevs to share what you’re working on. We can’t wait to see what you build! </p><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/GDBcode/~4/2jMyrlXiS1Y\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\"/>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Thu, 18 Jun +0000","feedId":10167,"bgimg":"https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-VNmy5ycvBjA/Xuex_FZrrVI/AAAAAAAAI5k/Jcxx3ItolWYfgAtydRStO11Z0aDNdIgjQCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/MistralAoGH.jpeg","linkMd5":"782e90518cac87867e4566f79984f7d9","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn38@2020_4/2020/08/25/00-46-09-996_e6e188168ac6a108.webp","destWidth":962,"destHeight":542,"sourceBytes":30248,"destBytes":15770,"author":"Google Developers","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-VNmy5ycvBjA/Xuex_FZrrVI/AAAAAAAAI5k/Jcxx3ItolWYfgAtydRStO11Z0aDNdIgjQCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/MistralAoGH.jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn38@2020_4/2020/08/25/00-46-09-996_e6e188168ac6a108.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/GDBcode/~4/2jMyrlXiS1Y":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn65@2020_3/2020/08/25/00-46-37-310_87714ce5e37d7251.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1598316369798},{"createdTime":"2020-08-25 08:46:09","updatedTime":"2020-08-25 08:46:09","title":"Future-Proofing Payments in an Uncertain World | Virtual Fireside Chat with Checkout.com CTO Riaz Bordie","link":"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/GDBcode/~3/iICmu4WCko0/future-proofing-payments-in-uncertain-world.html","description":"<meta name=\"twitter:image\" content=\"https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-SScTeHuUwqc/XvuVMXCJpgI/AAAAAAAAJDg/uabVeL_I_g4jvm1k9CjUp_8h4Wgau9RLQCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/googlepaycheckout.png\"><img style=\"display:none\" src=\"https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-SScTeHuUwqc/XvuVMXCJpgI/AAAAAAAAJDg/uabVeL_I_g4jvm1k9CjUp_8h4Wgau9RLQCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/googlepaycheckout.png\"> <p><em>Posted by Jose Ugia and Checkout.com</em><p><a href=\"https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-SScTeHuUwqc/XvuVMXCJpgI/AAAAAAAAJDg/uabVeL_I_g4jvm1k9CjUp_8h4Wgau9RLQCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/googlepaycheckout.png\" imageanchor=\"1\" ><img border=\"0\" id=\"imgFull\" src=\"https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-SScTeHuUwqc/XvuVMXCJpgI/AAAAAAAAJDg/uabVeL_I_g4jvm1k9CjUp_8h4Wgau9RLQCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/googlepaycheckout.png\" data-original-width=\"1600\" data-original-height=\"604\" /></a> <p>We sat down with Riaz Bordie, the CTO of Checkout.com, a leading international provider of online payment solutions, to get his advice to merchants and the developer community on how to think about future-proofing payments in the uncertain world we live in today. </p><p><strong>Jose Ugia: What advice do you have for merchants and developers as it relates to payments in these difficult times? </strong></p><p>Riaz: Merchants are seeing a polarizing impact of COVID-19 on their businesses. For those who have an online presence, you’re either seeing a lull in traffic or a spike. </p><p><em>If you’re a merchant who’s seeing traffic dwindle</em>, it’s more important than ever to make sure every transaction counts. If you used to see 50 transactions a day and now you see 10, you want to make sure all 10 deliver. Work with your Payment Service Provider (PSP) to make sure your approval ratios are as optimal as possible -- a legitimate customer who gets declined incorrectly may not return to purchase as they have in the past. If your PSP supports alternative payment methods like Google Pay that decrease friction at checkout and local payment methods if you’re selling internationally, that’s ideal. Keep an eye on your PSP’s stacks and uptimes to make sure you’re not missing out on sales due to outages or technical issues.  </p><p><em>If you’re a merchant seeing a spike in traffic</em>, that’s great news! But it’s important to note that a sudden traffic increase without proper operational and infrastructure planning can lead to fraud spikes, decreases in approval ratios, and downtime. With higher sales velocity, risk related issues will multiply.  You’ll see more attempted fraud as fraudsters take advantage of unsuspecting consumers, higher payment declines resulting from outdated issuer risk modeling and excessive chargeback levels, subscription cancellations, buyer’s remorse, among others. How are your payments infrastructure and operations equipped to handle all of this? </p><p>Make sure your infrastructure is capable of scaling up. If you don’t have autoscaling, you’ll need a team and processes in place to scale infrastructure for traffic spikes, and keep in mind this may get harder with people working remotely. Work your PSP and other providers to optimize your payments, risk models and chargeback handling during this challenging time. </p><p>For both types of merchants,  it’s important to pay closer attention to  performance of your payments system. This includes both ensuring that processes are working in an optimal way - especially given remote working situations and also ensuring that you are seeing efficiencies at scale. </p><p><strong>Jose Ugia: How did you think about building a payments infrastructure that was scalable and future-proof at Checkout.com? </strong></p><p>We knew in the beginning we wanted a unified API, which through a single integration gives a merchant access to any market via a range of payment methods and other facilities. We’ve worked hard to get acquiring licenses in as many markets as possible so we can bring acquiring in-house, which in turn gives us greater visibility on the entire payment flow. We have also invested in a gateway that can be consistently deployed in local geographies so that whether the merchant is in Dubai or Singapore, they are getting the most optimal traffic flow.  </p><p>Any engineer knows that tech breaks. Those who win have a better plan for dealing with breakage efficiently, to consistently maintain high levels of service. We spend a lot of time and resources on making sure our stack is resilient and we have the right operational processes in place to both proactively monitor for potential issues and respond correctly when they come up.  </p><p><strong>Jose Ugia: Speaking of where things are headed, where do you see the future of payments going from a payment service provider perspective?</strong></p><p>A few key trends I see: </p><p><em>Risk & Fraud Detection</em>. AI/ML is improving every aspect of tech. Fraudsters will get smarter but so will fraud prevention - it’s a cat and mouse game. In payments, sophisticated risk engines offering ML-based transaction scoring and highly customizable rules builders, among other features, will get better at detecting fraud without compromising sales.  </p><p><em>Global acceptance will continue to be complex but paramount. </em>Offering a variety of payment methods is table stakes these days. More and more, we’ll see that local payment methods aren’t the alternative but instead the primary way consumers pay. For example, you need to have Giropay if you’re selling in Germany and Alipay if you’re selling in China if you want a high conversion rate.  Ensure that you and your local entities have an optimized setup with your acquirer (ideally domestic where possible) focused on achieving the lowest costs and highest approval rates. </p><p><em>Embedded infrastructure. </em>Merchants - especially enterprise players - will want increased visibility and more control on optimizing their payment systems. We offer this level of insight and flexibility to our merchants today via our APIs around risk, reconciliation, disputes, etc. But we’re headed toward a world where dedicated infrastructure will become part of the package and allow for complete data separation and zero contention. </p><p><strong>Jose Ugia: How do you think these changes of payments infrastructure will impact consumers downstream?</strong></p><p>Convenience is king among consumers. I believe that COVID-19 will accelerate the move toward a contactless payments society, with consumers relying more on digital wallets and opportunities to pay through their devices. I personally no longer take my wallet out with me when I leave the house. A couple of years ago that felt like a conscious decision - now it’s just part of everyday life to rely solely on my smartphone to pay. </p><p>In some regions like MENA, which has typically been a cash-on-delivery society, we’re seeing more merchants close off cash and impose digital payments, opening up more adoption of upfront e-commerce payments. As mandated payment methods begin to change consumer behavior (studies say it takes 2 months to change a habit), new ways of paying will be here to stay, even beyond COVID-19. </p><br></br><center>- - - - - - - - - - - </center><br></br><i>Interested in learning more about Checkout.com’s services or speaking to a payments expert on how to optimize your payments stack? <a href=\"https://go.checkout.com/lead-gen/google-pay-blog-interest-capture\">Contact us here</a>. For Google Pay related requests and questions or to start your Google Pay integration, visit the <a href=\"https://pay.google.com/business/console?utm_source=google_dev_blog&utm_medium=article&utm_campaign=business_console_launchGoogle Pay Business Console.\">Google Pay Business Console.</a> </i><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/GDBcode/~4/iICmu4WCko0\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\"/>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Thu, 02 Jul 2020 14:53:00 data-original-height=\"1472\" /></a><p><a href=\"https://developers.google.com/community/dsc\">Google Developer Student Clubs</a> (DSC) are university based community groups for students who are interested in Google’s developer technologies. Each year, Google puts a call out to the entire DSC global community, asking students to answer one simple question: Can you solve a local problem in your community by building with Google’s technologies?   </p><p>This event is known as the DSC Solution Challenge and this year’s winners went above and beyond to answer the call - so much so that we couldn’t just pick one winner, we chose 10.  </p><p>While we initially thought we were the ones sending out the challenge, these young developers instead flipped the script back on us. Through their innovative designs and uncompromised creative spirit, they’ve pushed our team here at Google to stretch our thinking about how developers can build a more hopeful future.  </p><p>With this, we’re welcoming these passionate students and anyone interested to the virtual Solution Challenge Demo Day on August 26th, where the students will present their winning ideas in detail.  </p><p>Ahead of the event, learn more about this incredible group of thinkers and their solutions below.  </p> <h2>1. FreeSpeak - Technical University of Munich, Germany</h2><p>Maria Pospelova, Wei Wen Qing, and Almo Gunadya Sutedjo developed FreeSpeak, a software that uses modern machine learning and video/audio analyzing tools by leveraging TensorFlow and Google Cloud’s Natural Language to analyze presentations and give individual feedback and tips as a “virtual coach.”   </p><iframe id=\"imgFull\" width=\"560\" height=\"315\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/xYmyODdRSCw\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen></iframe><center><p><i>“We’ve loved connecting with talented people from around the world and exchanging ideas with them. We see that we can provide impact not only to our local neighborhood, but also around the world and help people. This motivates us to work a lot harder.”</i></p></center> <h2>2. CoronaAI - University of California Berkeley, United States</h2><p>Anushka Purohit, Anupam Tiwari, and Neel Desai created CoronaAI, a TensorFlow based technology that helps examine COVID-19 data. Specifically, the device is made up of a band worn around a patient's chest that uses electrodes to extract real-time images of the lungs. From here, the band connects to a monitor that allows doctors to examine patients in real time without being near them.</p><iframe width=\"560\" height=\"315\" id=\"imgFull\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/TvKnGL0Nr6w\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen></iframe><center><p><i>“We're honestly huge fans of the Google Cloud Platform because of its simplicity, familiarity, and the large number of resources available. Developing this project was the best learning experience.”</i></p></center> <h2>3. Worthy Walk - National University of Computer & Emerging Sciences, Pakistan</h2><p>Syed Moazzam Maqsood, Krinza Momin, Muhammad Ahmed Gul, and Hussain Zuhair built <a href=\"http://www.worthywalkapp.com/\">Worthy Walk</a>: an Android and iOS app that provides its users a platform to achieve health goals by walking, running, or cycling. To encourage users, Worthy Walk provides an inbuilt currency called Knubs that can be redeemed as discounts from local businesses, shops, and startups. </p><iframe id=\"imgFull\" width=\"560\" height=\"315\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/eKhv4dd_LGo\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen></iframe><center><p><i>“Being a part of DSC means friendship - sharing knowledge and resources - all while developing a social infrastructure that gives people the power to build a global community that works for all of us.”</i></p></center> <h2>4. Simhae : Deep sea of mind - Soonchunhyang University, South Korea</h2><p>Yuna Kim, Young hoon Jo, Jeong yoon Joo, and Sangbeom Hwang created Simhae, a platform created with Flutter and Google Cloud that allows users to access basic information and activities to inspire them to attend self-help gatherings run by suicide prevention centers. They believe that this experience is an important point that can lead to solidarity of suicide survivors. </p><iframe id=\"imgFull\" width=\"560\" height=\"315\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/UIexXnfIUqM\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen></iframe><center><p><i>“It's so nice to have a chance to meet more diverse people. Through these communities, I can make up for my shortcomings and share more information with those who have different experiences than me - all while developing my own potential.”</i></p></center> <h2>5. Emergency Response Assistance - University of Education, Winneba (College of Technology Kumasi), Ghana</h2><p>Elvis Antwi Sarfo, Yaw Barnieh Anane, Ampomah Ata Acheampong Prince, and Perditha Abena Acheampong constructed Emergency Response Assistance, an Android application to help health authorities post the latest first aid steps to educate the public and also help the victims report emergency cases with a click of a button. The Emergency Response team will also be able to track the exact location of the victims on the map. </p><iframe id=\"imgFull\" width=\"560\" height=\"315\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/oLjyFD3B5eo\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen></iframe><center><p><i>“DSC is not just a community, it’s an inspiration. It’s outstanding how the platform has brought all of these students, lecturers, and teaching assistants, who are all so passionate about using tech to solve problems, together.”</i></p></center> <h2>6. Tulibot - Politeknik Elektronika Negeri Surabaya, Indonesia</h2><p>Muhammad Alan Nur, Pravasta Caraka Bramastagiri, Eva Rahmadanti, and Namira Rizqi Annisa created Tulibot: an integrated assistive technology, built with the Google Speech API, that’s made to bridge communication between deaf people and society. The group made two main devices, Smart Glasses and Smart Gloves. Smart Glasses help with communication for the hearing impaired by showing real time answers directly on the glasses from its interlocutors. Smart Gloves transcribe gesture input into audio output by implementing gesture to text technology.</p> <iframe width=\"560\" id=\"imgFull\" height=\"315\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/CUNms3gso-o\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen></iframe> <center><p><i>“This has been an amazing opportunity for us because with this challenge, we can learn many things like coding, management, business, and more. The special materials we can get directly from Google is so helpful.”</i></p></center> <h2>7. Picare - The Hong Kong University of Science & Technology,  Hong Kong</h2><p>Sze Yuk Yin, Kwok Ue Nam, Ng Chi Ting, Chong Cheuk Hei, and Silver Ng developed Picare, a healthcare matching platform built with Flutter and Google Machine Learning to help elderly people in Hong Kong. Users will be able to use the app to research, schedule, and pay caregivers directly through the app. </p><iframe id=\"imgFull\" width=\"560\" height=\"315\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/uM5vLz4qzoY\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen></iframe><center><p><i>“Our community hosted several workshops ranging from design thinking to coding techniques.
